# 道门定制

**Daoist Ritual Regulations**

**Title:** *Daoist Ritual Regulations*
**Original Compilation:** *Collected and Compiled by Lü Yuansu of the Song Dynasty, Edited by Hu Xianglong*
**Ten volumes**
**Source of the Base Text:** *The Standard Daoist Canon (正统道藏)* Volume One (正一部)

**Contents:**

**Preface**
**Volume One:**
*On Petitions and Memorials*
*On Addressing the Sovereign as "臣" (Chén, "Subject")*
*On Petitions from the "众真" (Zhòngzhēn, "Assemblies of Perfected Ones")*
*On Official Documents (文牒, Wéndiè)*
*On the Edict to Female Perfected Ones (女青) and the Imperial Jewel Edict (宝诰, Bǎogǎo)*

*On Terminology and Meanings (词意, Cíyì)*
*On the Metrical Form of the *Xuandu Regulations* (玄都律议章词体, Xuāndū Lǜ Yìzhāng cí tǐ)*

*On Titles in the Taqing (太清) System*
*On Petitions from the "众真" (Zhòngzhēn, "Assemblies of Perfected Ones")*

*On Terminology and Script (字体, Zìtǐ)*

*On Announcing the Taqing Titles (宣读太清衔, Xuāndú Tàqīng Xiàn)*
*On the Rituals of the Imperial Consorts (后宫曹, Hòugōng Cáo)*

**On the Dao/Way’s Simplicity and Ritual’s Completeness**

The Dao/Way is most simple, yet ritual is most elaborate.
All that humankind uses to serve Heaven is the Dao/Way.
When serving Heaven, one cultivates the utmost sincerity—
and within this, ritual is preserved.
This is the fundamental intent of the Sage’s teachings for the world.

Yet between excess and deficiency,
one must strike a balanced mean—
neither extreme is permissible.

The Dao/Way’s fasting and ritual petitions (*zhāijiào*) originally required only seals and vermilion stamps.
Other documents—petitions, memorials, and official dispatches—
were later additions, blending secular customs with scriptural precepts.

Since there is no fixed standard,
some may err toward excessive detail,
losing the essence of simplicity—
leaving those of lesser means unable to comply;
or they may act recklessly,
causing those who earnestly serve Heaven
to lack proper guidance,
displeasing their intent.

I, Brú Yuánsù, have long been troubled by this.
I now seek to establish a standardized system,
so that neither omission nor excess may occur—
that the simple may not be obscured,
nor the elaborate overreach—
thus ensuring that the rites of serving Heaven and the Dao/Way
are not arbitrarily diminished or inflated by human whims.

Further clarifications are provided below.
Let those capable of discernment examine them.

**Recorded in the Year of the Monkey, Chúnxī Stele (淳熙戊申)**
By the Daoist of Táng’ān, Jiang Pǔ’ān, **Lǚ Yuánsù**

**Volume One of *Standardized Dao/Way Procedures***
Compiled by the Daoist of Xīshǔ, Pǔ’ān Lǚ Yuánsù
Edited by Zhūlíng Zhēnxuàn Xìngqí Hú Xiānglóng

**On the Regulation of Petitions and Memorials**

**On the Regulation of Petitions and Memorials**

For the **Nine Sovereigns’ Petitions**, each should submit a single memorial, briefly stating the purpose and requesting a date and time for the **ritual offering and descent of the True Ones**, expressing the hope for imperial favor—without necessarily detailing all wishes.

For other petitions from the **Celestial Worthies**, as well as memorials from the **Three Realms and lands**, the same applies. The actual invocation and supplication will be handled through the prescribed liturgical texts once the altar is established.

If conducting a **ritual offering**, submit only one memorial. For petitions to the **Sages**, a simple request statement suffices. Listing the **Nine Sovereigns’ titles** in a memorial violates proper form.

**On Addressing the Sovereigns:**
Beyond the **Nine Sovereigns**, other Sages should not be addressed as *"Your Subject."* The Nine Sovereigns are akin to the supreme ruler among mortals, while even those Sages holding imperial rank govern only their respective domains—like vassals and officials to the Nine Sovereigns.

For **High Functionaries’ memorials**, if the **ritual master’s name** is included, the character *"subject"* should be omitted. Similarly, within the **ritual master’s liturgical text**, the High Functionary’s name should not be followed by *"subject."*

**On Petitions from the Celestial Worthies:**
The **Yellow Register’s Thousand-Two-Hundred Celestial Worthies of the Luo Heaven**, though many in number, cannot all be individually petitioned. Instead, select from the **Three Sovereigns’ scriptures** those Worthies already invoked, drafting **three memorials to the Three Sovereigns**, humbly requesting that the **Three Sovereign Emperors and the assembled Worthies descend in person.** The same applies to memorials from the **Three Realms.** Thus, petitions may be transmitted systematically without redundancy, ensuring comprehensive coverage.

**On Liturgical Documents and Memorials:**
The **Celestial Master’s chief disciples**, who also lead the **Heavenly Pivot Bureau of Petitions**, must oversee all memorials addressed to the Nine Sovereigns, submitting them first to the **Heavenly Pivot Academy.** All official correspondence must bear the title **"Great Mysterious Bureau."** After the altar is established, the **Celestial Master’s title** must be honored first, followed by the **High Functionary’s title** in proper order. This follows the **Celestial Master’s legacy**, passed down to ensure communication with both the seen and unseen realms—an ancient practice now often neglected. Recently, some omit *"altar established"* after the Celestial Master’s title, falsely implying the document originates directly from Heaven. Additionally, appending the High Functionary’s name as a postscript for execution is improper. It is better to adhere to the ancient method. Now, even within the Celestial Master’s memorials, we include the **request for rank and position**, ensuring personal intentions are fully expressed.

**On the Female Qing-Shao Scriptures and Precious Edicts:**
The recorded **"Mixed Void’s Crimson Text of Primordial Sovereign Edicts"** is part of the **Female Qing’s laws.** When drafting memorials for promotions or transfers, it suffices to invoke the **Great Mysterious Bureau’s ritual offering**, seating the deities as prescribed. Recently, some treat these as imperial edicts, requiring **decrees and rescripts**, crafting elaborate paired phrases and establishing new formats, such as:
*"From the Three Heavenly Gates, in accordance with the decree received."*

Others expand with multiple clauses, resembling imperial amnesties—**not only improper but entirely fabricated**, violating doctrinal principles. Furthermore, the **East Peak Sovereign** oversees mortal souls and governs the **Earthly Spirits**, so when extracting souls, a memorial must be submitted to the East Peak, requesting the **Earth and Water Departments** to issue confirmation. Some draft memorials from the **East Peak, Earthly Waters, City Gods, and all subterranean deities**, leading to excessive disorder. This stems from human assumptions that deities cannot simultaneously perceive all places at once. Yet in the unseen realm, divine influence acts without delay, requiring no human calculation.

The **"Living Heaven’s Precious Edicts"** also improperly mimic imperial rescripts and petitions, recorded as **"received by decree"**—not only inviting ridicule but also burdening the teachings.

**On the Golden Register and White Tablets:**
The **White Tablets’ efficacy in benefiting the unseen** is too vast to fully describe. Only **Zhang Lihua’s case** is clearly documented: when reciting the **Nine Passages**, coinciding with the moment of repentance, burning the tablets immediately ensures the petition reaches its intended moment of merit completion. Recently, some burn **salvation-sufficiency talismans** at the very moment of petition, claiming this allows the deceased to escape hell—**this is incorrect.** The **extraction of souls** relies on proper memorials and white tablets, to be proclaimed during the **transmission of the Dao**, so that the deceased may benefit from the **merits generated at the altar**, as well as the **vows of keeping precepts, repentance, and renewal of life.** Only then should the tablets be offered to the **Ten Directions**, granting pardon and resolving grievances. **This is the true path to escaping hell and ascending to the Vermilion Palace.** Thus, the scripture states:
*"The beings of the Nine Dark Realms, hearing the Northern Emperor’s broad petitions, generate remorse and seek liberation. The Celestial Venerable then instructs them in precepts and grants talismans—this is most verifiable."*

As for **reciting spells, inscribing talismans, and drafting memorials**, these are not difficult. Mastering **twenty talismans** allows for memorization, as their meanings align. Those who test this will find the claim true.

**On Liturgical Phrasing.**

「On **Liturgical Phrasing**,
the **Blue Scripts** should be addressed solely to the **Three Pure Ones** and the **Jade Emperor**,** or exclusively to the **Jade Emperor** for greater efficacy. Some may extend to the **Nine Sovereigns** and below, even to the **Ten Extremes** of all **Celestial Beings**, **Three Realms’ True Spirits**,** and others listed within the **Scripts**. Yet how can one petition the **Supreme Emperor** and then sequentially inform all **True Spirits**? Again, the **Scripts** composed by the imperial court typically consist of no more than **sixty or seventy characters**, without the need for **intermediate invocations** or **prostrations**. This demonstrates that the **formats** of **Scriptural Tablets** are indeed **meticulous and solemn**.

Moreover, the **Scripts** should first express **sincere vows**, then directly present the matter at hand. Since **parallel structure** and **paired phrasing** are not feasible, though it may be convenient to recite them aloud, the **Script’s text** should still employ **paired structure** and **repetition** to ensure **precision and solemnity**. In the **vows**, there is no need to enumerate all the **rites performed at the altar**; the **Meritorious Sutra** can suffice. It merely states: *“On such-and-such a day and hour, we begin the rites; on such-and-such a day and hour, we complete the **memorial offering** and disperse the assembly.”* Thus, the **Script** should outline the **progressive recitation of meritorious deeds**, lest the **language grow stale** and weary the listeners. Once the **vows** are fully detailed in the **Script**, only a **concise, heartfelt passage** should follow to convey the **urgent sincerity**.

In the past, there were **rituals performed at each of the Nine Hours**, with **descriptions of the scene** inscribed in the **Scripts**, though these were mere **formalities**. Now, for the **Yellow Scripts**,** the rites conducted during the **Nine Hours of Sutra Recitation** should each be recorded in a separate **Script**, ensuring that the **rituals and recitations** align in **meaning and intent**. This also reflects the **universality of the officiant’s vows**—for **state, family, living and deceased, dragons, spirits, and lands**—as well as the **original, heartfelt purpose** of the **Scripts**.

As for **memorial rites**,** it is best to use only **opening and closing vows**. Further, those who inscribe **Scripts** on **yellow paper** are acting improperly. How can **subjects’ petitions** be written on **yellow paper**? The **Blue Scripts** with **red inscriptions** symbolize **sincerity akin to offering one’s liver and shedding blood**. The **Laws of the Mystic Capital** on **Scriptural Phrasing** decree:
*"The **form of Scriptural Phrasing** should be **substantial yet unadorned**, **crude yet not clumsy**, **plain yet not vulgar**, **authentic yet not false**, **direct yet not oblique**, **persuasive yet not verbose**, **refined yet not impure**, **pure yet not turbid**, **upright yet not deviant**, **concise yet sincere**—then it can **move Heaven and Earth, stir spirits and deities**, and **directly ascend to the Celestial Bureaus**, with **retribution and response arriving swiftly**. Violators shall be **punished by the officials of the **Non-Conformity Bureau**.**

**On the Title of the **Supreme Clarity** (太清衔):**
The **Supreme Clarity Title** consists of **fifty-two characters**, arranged to form a **rectangle of two inches by four fingers’ breadth**. Each character must be **clearly distinguishable and legible**; characters should not be **overlapped**. Some may hastily reduce it to **one inch by two fingers’ breadth**, which is no different from **smearing and erasing**. Others may stretch the characters **too long or too sparse**, violating the **prescribed standards**. All who oversee the **Scriptural Titles** must adhere to **meticulous solemnity**, ensuring they are **uniform, precise, and not carelessly simplified**. Among the **rites**, the **Jade Seal** holds the most **prohibitive weight**.

According to the **Essentials of the **Jade Cavern**’s Teachings** by the **Three Caverns Masters**:
*"The **Supreme Clarity Title** must be inscribed **without delay**. When the time for the rites arrives, the **Title** should be written and placed in a **box** to await the performance."*

**On the **True Spirits’ Memorial Tablets:**
The **Three Scripts** and all **memorial rites** involve descending **True Spirits**, each with **distinct ranks**. These ranks must not be **transgressed**. In the **Golden Script** rites, only **one sheet of paper money** per **True Spirit** is offered, without combining their **sacred titles**. Now, we take **one thousand two hundred** **True Spirits’ sacred titles**, verify and arrange them by **rank**, ensuring **no irreverence**. For **rites of disaster alleviation** or **oath-taking**,** the **True Spirits** should be petitioned **as appropriate**, following this model, and **no more than one hundred twenty** should be included. Those who manage the **Scriptural Titles** should first prepare a **single copy of the **Sacred Titles****, which the **High Master** seals and the **Grand Lecturer** then invokes, ensuring **harmony in descent**. Otherwise, the **High Master**, the **Grand Lecturer**, and the **Memorial Tablets** will be **utterly disconnected**.

**On the **Dragon Tablets:**
In ancient times, when **Daoist adepts** began their **cultivation**, they first sent **petitionary Tablets** to the **Three Offices**—**Heavenly, Earthly, and Watery Offices**—to **seek the removal of sins and the recording of merits**, hence the phrase *“vows to the gods, transmission of vows.”* Earlier sages took this from the **Three Scripts’ altar rites**, where after completing the **memorial offering**, they **reiterated their vows**, which was also a **commendable practice**.

The **Tablets** should be made of **carved wood**, symbolizing **purity**. According to the ***Materia Medica**,** the **wood of the **Mallow** (木槿)** resembles a small **hollyhock**,** with **pale red** flowers, **five petals** per bloom, which **open in the morning and close by evening**. Its wood is **white and lustrous**, hence its use, and its name carries the **sound of solemnity**. The **Tablets** are borne by a **golden dragon**.

Further, the **Tablets’ length and breadth** should be mirrored in an **empty central plaque**, with the **dragon’s base** depicted at the bottom to **position the Tablet**. Some may use the **Earthly Office’s dragon**, which is **seated to subdue the home**, though this is merely **common belief**. The phrase *“golden dragon delivering the Tablets”* implies that a **seated dragon** could **transmit and place** them—how absurd!

**Green silk** is used to **symbolize severed hair**, with **each Tablet** requiring **twenty-four feet**. The **Tablets** are tied to the **dragon’s reins** with **three sets of **golden buttons****, totaling **twenty-one orifices**, and **seven orifices** per **Tablet**. These are **knotted onto the silk** to represent the **dragon’s bit and bridle**, embodying **firmness and respect**, and **precious jade** is added to **signify reverence and heavy offerings**.

The **jewel of the **Heavenly Office** is **round and green**, the **jewel of the **Earthly Office** is **square and yellow**, and the **jewel of the **Watery Office** is **dark and six-pointed**. These symbols reflect the **numerological essence** of **water**—**level, empty, and rising**.

The **sacred titles** of the **Nine Sovereigns**, such as **Grace, Pardon, Original Forgiveness, Heavenly Might, Discernment, Descent, Sutra Teachings, Stormy Command, and Sacred Virtue**,** are all **level and unobstructed**. If petitioning the **Nine Sovereigns’ Scriptural Titles** or similar, and the **Script** contains **sequential True Spirits’ names**, only **one character** should be **levelled**. If exclusively petitioning **sequential True Spirits**, all characters must be **levelled**. For **land deities and lesser spirits**, no characters need be **levelled**. If the **format** includes **round hollows**, these too are **empty of one character**. **Levelled characters** are all **hollowed by one stroke**. If the **Script** contains **sequential sacred titles** or **documents** with the **Nine Sovereigns’ or higher sacred titles**, all must be **levelled**.

Additionally, **Scriptural Titles** must not **break or omit names**; other **Scriptural documents** should also **avoid such omissions**, adjusting instead to ensure **names appear only in a single line** for the best effect.»

「Proposing the Establishment of *Jiao* Rites to Invite the True Spirits

For *Jiao* rites held within the **Great Inner Daoist Assembly** or in the **Eastern and Southern regions**, the practice is simply to establish the *Jiao* rites. At the appointed time for offerings, one must still prepare the **ritual implements** according to the **rank of the True Spirits** being invited.

During the **invitation of True Spirits**, when tea is served and the **three offerings** are completed, the **sacred titles** must be addressed with **proper reverence**, and the **sacrificial soup** must be presented with **careful deliberation** and **supreme sincerity**—this is most fitting in terms of ritual propriety.

Indeed, the **opening of the altar** is a declaration of the **fast**. Conducting the **Daoist rites** at each hour is to maintain a **sincere heart** during the fast and to **uphold repentance** through ritual practice. Only after **accumulating merit and fulfilling duties**—when the Daoist rites are complete—does one then rely on this **virtuous power** to **invite the True Spirits**, partake in this **sincere offering**, and conclude the **fast’s merit**.

This is why, before the rites begin, one first requests the **Five Teachers** to bear witness—this is precisely the reasoning behind it.

However, even **120 ritual portions** can be sufficiently prepared. As for **1,200 portions**, the **implements and offerings** become somewhat excessive. Yet if one can simply **increase the ritual implements**, the rites may still proceed, for the essence lies in the **clarity of intent** in the *Jiao* and fast.

Thus, it is stated: *“To establish a certain Daoist Assembly and hold a grand *Jiao* on the [appointed] day, the number of portions for this single session is as follows.”* In **Sichuan’s Daoist rites**, from the **opening of the altar** until the **third hour** or **ninth hour**, offerings are already made during the **Daoist rites**.

The **ritual officers**, having already exerted themselves in labor and fatigue, reach the moment of **inviting the True Spirits** and the **three offerings**, when **heavenly and human beings resonate in harmony**. Often, they are exhausted and cannot fully express their sincerity. How much better it would be to conduct the **Daoist rites over three days** or even **one day**, focusing solely on **devotion**, **incense and fire**, and **cultivating the spirit** to seek **true communion**, thereby **fulfilling the rites with utmost sincerity and diligence** at the time of the *Jiao*—would this not be ideal?

The **proposed document** for submission states: *“When submitting petitions, the intent is to fulfill the devout’s wish to serve Heaven without waste, and to ensure that those performing the rites are not burdened by errors in the petitions.”* When **Daoist novices** hold the pen, they should be able to **grasp the principles** of the rites, **correctly render the characters**, and **align the mundane with the sacred**—thus qualifying them for the **rank of *zān-hè* (道童, Daoist acolyte)**. In the future, should they assist others in conducting *Jiao* rites or submitting petitions, their **calligraphy will conform to the script**, which is also a matter worthy of consideration within the Daoist tradition.

In one action, all three aspects—**fulfillment of the devout’s wish**, **prevention of ritual errors**, and **qualification of novices**—are benefitted.

Some may argue: *“This proposed document, though early in formulation, can still be used. But how does it justify the advancement of pen-holding Daoists to the *zān-hè* rank? Why should it be included among beneficial matters?”*

The reply is: *“No, that is not correct.”* Though this document may seem **detailed and thorough**, it still **depends on Daoists to adjust according to circumstances**, weighing what is **heavy or light** in ritual propriety. If the devout **wholeheartedly prepare offerings** and **serve Heaven with the Dao**, will they not surpass this?

If such rites were conducted by **lowly scribes**, I would not recognize their **true devotion to Heaven**—let alone speak further.

**Regarding the Correction of Character Forms**

There are **characters penned freely by past masters** and those **convenient for common use**. Variations in strokes and additions/subtractions are **unacceptable in ritual petitions**—only the **Sichuan standard** should be employed, as it is **proper and conventional**.

Even if **commonly misused characters** are listed here for reference, their inclusion is **well-intentioned**. However, some **obscure ancient characters** are occasionally used, **rarely seen in the world**, and **scattered without clear citation**, making them ultimately **difficult to locate or select**.

Common characters are also numerous, **intermingled within the text**, yet this is not ideal. Now, I have **compiled and standardized the character forms** as corrected by **earlier Daoist scholars**, ensuring that **from beginning to end**, all characters are **properly rendered**.

Within the collection, **commonly misused characters** have been **removed**, and their meanings **corrected**, so that those **copying the text** may **sacrifice to the celestial hosts**, **report to the Three Realms’ True Spirits**, and upon opening the volume, **clearly perceive** the **unmistakable and easily discernible** characters.

Thus, **no ancient characters obscure the meaning**, nor **common errors mislead the reader**—this can be said to **fulfill both excellence and beauty**.

**Explanation of the *Tàiqīng* Title, the True Spirits, and the Days *Wùxū* and *Wùchén***

Recently, some have claimed there is **no Heavenly Sovereign** (天帝丈人) and thus **omitted its mention**. However, they **do not know** that **Confucian scholars** must **recite the classics** before they can **be called Confucian**.

According to the *Xuandu Ritual* (玄都律), the *Chisongzi Chapter of Ritual Observances* (赤松子章历), the *Excerpts on Precepts and Rituals* (戒律钞), and the *Secrets of Ascension and Concealment* (登真隐诀), it is recorded that on **days *Wùxū* (戊戌) and *Wùchén* (戊辰)**, the **Most Venerable Sovereign** (太上丈人) and the **Most Venerable Sovereign of *Tàiqīng*** (太清丈人)—the **most exalted** among them—**attend the Most Venerable Laozi** (太上老君). The **Most Venerable Sovereign of *Tàiqīng*** is the **exalted one** of the **Eastern Palace**, who **supervises the registration of all men and women** destined to be born, **inscribing their names in the Jade Ledger** (玉历).

The **Nine *Qi* Sovereign** (九炁丈人) is also a **Most Venerable Sovereign of *Tàiqīng***, overseeing the **affairs of ghosts and spirits**, and **attends the Nine Old Immortals of the Eastern Palace** (九老仙都君). The **Eastern Palace of *Tàiqīng*** is not the **Eastern Palace of *Xuánzhōu*** (玄洲), and it is responsible for **registering all men and women** destined to die, **recording their names in the Ledger of Death** (死籍).

The **Heavenly Sovereign** (天帝丈人) is mentioned in the *Xuandu Ritual* as **attending the Heavenly Sovereign** (天帝君), who is the **one sovereign of the Eastern Palace** in *Tàiqīng*—and he is tasked with **registering men and women** who have **committed offenses**, **degrees of punishment** in the **Right Contract** (右契).

These are all **sacred titles** of the **Three Heavens of *Tàiqīng*’s Eastern Palace**, related to the **petitions submitted to the True Spirits**. The **Heavenly Master** (天师) **returns to the Celestial Register** (天曹), **examines and selects** those whose names remain, **distinguishing good from evil**.

On these days, the **Heavenly Gate** is **closed**, and the **Earthly Portals** are **sealed**; all **external affairs are suspended**, and **no petitions may be submitted**. If a **auspicious day** occurs, one may **submit a petition for merit**. For on the **Great Day of Celebration**, **officials, soldiers, and deities** **universally confer merit and rewards**.

No other petitions may be submitted; **violators** will be **punished with 100 days of calamity**. It is also said: *“If on these days one encounters the **Three Celestial Gatherings** (三元), **Three Celestial Assemblies** (三会), **Eight Festivals** (八节), or one’s **natal day** (本命), these may still be submitted without restriction, for this day **specifically permits human repentance**.”*

On other days, **petitions are not allowed**. Ancient scholars, when recording **year, month, and day**, would only note *“the Heavenly Gate opens”*—indicating that there are **other methods** for determining this. On **solar days** (陽日), specifically the **hours *Zǐ* (子) and *Yǐn* (寅)**, as well as *Wǔ* (午), *Shēn* (申), and *Xū* (戌)**, when it is **lunar nighttime**, the **Heavenly Gate opens**.

On **lunar days** (陰日), specifically the **hours *Yǒu* (酉) and *Hài* (亥)**, as well as *Chǒu* (丑), *Mǎo* (卯), *Wèi* (巳), *Wèi* (未), and *Yǒu* (酉)**, when it is **solar daytime**, the **Heavenly Gate opens**.

This distinction, **we must know**. Moreover, if **petition texts** contain **arbitrary alterations** that **obstruct the meaning**, one example is given here for reference.»

「On the *Shēngshénjīng* (生神經) preface, it states: *“In accordance with the proper **postures of reverence** (俯仰), the **sacred oaths** (盟真) are fully observed, facing south in a **prolonged kneeling posture** (長跪), to entrust to the **Flying Heavenly Supreme God-King** (飛天無極神王)—this is the matter in question.”* Yet recently, some have altered the original text without knowing its source, changing it to *“**deficient posture** (乏格), **lost posture** (亡格), **erroneous posture** (失格)”*—unaware that these words follow as a single phrase. They then arbitrarily modify and truncate the text below to suit their own interpretations, disregarding the **proper liturgical structure** (章法). This is clearly inappropriate.

Similarly, in the case of **reciting the *Tàiqīng* (太清) title**, according to the *Yǐn Zhēnrén Wènkē Jīng* (尹真人问科经) and the *Tiānshī Wènfǎ Jīng* (天师问法经), the **Celestial Master** (天师) asked **Laozi** (老君): *“There are those who finish reciting *Yǐn* (以聞) before reciting *Tàiqīng*; others who recite *Tàiqīng* after *Yǐn*; some who **prostrate and bow twice** (稽首再拜) before reciting the **fine characters of the *Tàiqīng* title** (太清衔细字), then reciting *Yǐn*, then their **surname** (臣姓); or those who recite *Tàiqīng* at the end. These practices differ—what is the correct method?”*

**Laozi** replied: *“After reciting *Yǐn*, one then recites their surname, then the *Tàiqīng* title, followed by the **yearly designation** (次年号), each separated by **three lines** (三行). This is the **fixed method** (不易之法) for writing the petitions.”*

**However, during the **solemn recitation** (宣读) of the *Tàiqīng* title**, one must first recite *Yǐn*, then **kneel in prolonged reverence** (長跪), holding the **tablet** (执版), before reciting the **fine characters of the *Tàiqīng* title**, then their **name and surname** (姓名), and finally the **yearly designation**. This is the **complete method of the Celestial Sovereign** (天帝具法). Recently, some have moved the *Tàiqīng* title before the surname in their written petitions, likely due to superficial understanding without careful examination. This **disrupts the liturgical order** (坏乱章法), causing those unfamiliar with the proper **scriptural conventions** (执笔不谙之者) to follow suit out of curiosity, without regard for **ritual censure** (阴责). Not only will such **petitions be rejected** (章奏遭却), but the **ritual officiants** (斋主), **Daoist clergy responsible for petitions** (道家司章奏者), and even the **officials of the Daoist scriptures** (章中官吏) will all face **punishment for improper conduct** (从坐之谴). Should this not be clarified and corrected?

**Regarding the **post-petition officials** (章后宫曹)**,** whether the ritual is grand or modest, the **most vital benefit** (莫大之利益) lies in the **proper composition and submission of petitions** (奏章). The **post-petition officials**, including the **monthly divisions of the Jade Maidens** (月分玉女), are outlined in the *Xuāndū Lǜ Zhèngyī Zhāngyí* (玄都律正一章仪) and its **key stipulations** (所修旨要), with all necessary details provided for reference. The **Celestial Sovereign** (太上) established the **Daoist teachings** (教) to be followed by all—how can they be treated so lightly?

If one does not adhere to the **proper ritual procedures** (仪), they will suffer the **punishment of having their lifespan reduced** (夺算扫除之罚) in this life and the **torment of sinking into the muddy path** (泥途奔溺之苦) after death. Recently, a single volume of **petition texts** (章文) was published, apparently to cater to the **preferences of novices** (徇道童之见), omitting the **post-petition officials and Jade Maidens** (宫曹玉女) for convenience. Yet they fail to realize that during **high-ranking ritual invocations** (伏章), one must **visualize the post-petition officials and Jade Maidens** (存想) before proceeding.

In the **collection of petition texts** (集中), the **three chapters on *Diānbá* (拔)、*Xiāozāi* (消灾)、and *Fēnjiě Zhǒngsòng* (分解冢讼)** are altered, with **small-character annotations** (小字笺注) often taken from **standardized Daoist compendia** (定制集). Some of these annotations are acceptable, while others are **open to debate** (可议). For instance, they **cite established precedents** (引定故事) to justify phrases like *“**reverence to the five deities** (对禺)”*—a practice that should be reconsidered.

Moreover, sincere **devotees** (至诚之士), who earnestly believe in the **Supreme Truths** (上真) and honor them accordingly, may be misled by such errors. Yet this is merely what the *Yìshèng Zhuàn* (翊圣传) refers to as **“transformed visions of Guānyīn** (化见观音)”**—**merely illusory manifestations.

**Regarding **documentary scripts** (文牒)**, the language of Daoist **petitions and memorials** (奏状) must be **pure and elegant** (清净典雅), employing **metamorphic phrases** (蝉蜕挟法) that align with the **Celestial Sovereign’s intent** (太上所以立教劝善之意). Yet some who specialize in **textual composition** (文字) have imitated the **style of official government documents** (官府行移), creating **petitions resembling mundane legal correspondence** (造为文牒公据之类). Their **coarse and improper language** (言词芜鄙) **offends the deities** (凌胁神祇), and the **titles of Celestial Master and High Functionary** (天师高功衔) are falsely appended at the end, **arising purely from their own whims** (出於己意). The deities are **omniscient and upright** (聪直)—how can they be deceived?

The **purpose of Daoist ritual** (奉道事天理趣) and the **meaning of Daoist scriptures** (考召治鬼) **differ fundamentally** from the **intentions of legal officials** (法官). Furthermore, the **conventions of government documentation** (官府文法) are **entirely unrelated**. Those who rely on such **improper compositions** (恃此一切施为) will inevitably face **ritual inconveniences** (不便). Some modifications may be necessary, but this must be handled by **scholars of profound insight** (高识之士) who carefully examine the matter before implementing any changes.

If **Elemental Master** (元素) has any observations, he will not **conceal them for personal gain** (秘为一己之私). Thus, he continues with these **four clarifications** (四说), aiming to **dispel obscurations** (祛障蔽) and **illuminate the teachings** (教明) with **persuasive language** (辞达). All **fellow Daoists** (同袍) and **those who revere the Dao** (崇设之家) must now **avoid ritual offenses** (无因斋获罪) from these errors.

**On the **Method of Writing Petitions** (书章法):**
The **scriptural precepts** (科) state: *“When writing petitions, face north and place the **tablet** (案) before you. The **brush and inkstone** (笔砚) must be **distinct and pure** (悉异), never used by others. Write while **sealing your *qi*** (闭炁), without speaking to anyone. Do not set down the **brush** (笔) before completing a character. Use **yellow silk paper** (黄素), ensuring it remains **unblemished and free from loss** (勿令破损飞落). Cut the paper on **clean, sacred ground** (床席地土上), making the **width one foot two inches** (幅广一尺二寸), the **line spacing one inch two divisions** (行阔一寸二分), and **seventeen characters per line** (行列一十七字). Leave **eight divisions of space** (上空八分) below the title, and ensure the **final line does not allow ants to pass beneath** (下不通走蚁).”*—though it is often mistakenly written as *“below allows ants to pass”* (下通走蚁). The **scriptures uniformly state** (诸经所载) that the **final line must not allow ants to pass beneath** (下不通走蚁).

The **character for “subject”** (臣) **must not appear at the beginning of a line**, nor the **character for “ghost”** (鬼) **as the first character**. Avoid **writing characters with unfinished strokes** (垂生) or **exposing characters with incomplete strokes** (露死), nor **dragging strokes that damage names** (抽破人姓名).

The **distance between *Yǐn* and the **double bow** (再拜) should be **one inch two divisions** (一寸二分). The **surname** (臣姓) should be **three lines below *Yǐn***. The *Tàiqīng* title should be **three lines below the surname**, and the **yearly designation** (太岁) **three lines below the *Tàiqīng* title**. After completing the text, **burn incense three times** (焚香三). Then, **re-examine the scripture** (点检), placing it in a **pure location** (净所) to await its **proper use in ritual** (行事). Failure to comply will result in **reduction of lifespan** (夺算).

*The above is extracted from **Daoist Canon: *Xuāndū Lǜ* (玄都律) and *Zhǐyào* (旨要)**.*」

**Daoist Canon: *Xuāndū Lǜ* (玄都律) and *Zhǐyào* (旨要)**

**The Supreme Lord’s *Yuan* (元) and *Zhang* (丈) Person’s Palace (虚元丈人宫):**
January, December

**The Palace of *Xuán Lǎo* (玄老) and the Daoist Capital of *Xiān Dū* (仙都宫):**
February

**The Palace of the Supreme Lord’s Three Heavens and *Tàiqīng* (太清宫):**
March, April

**The Palace of the Supreme Lord’s *Chóngdào* (重道宫):**
May

**The Palace of the Supreme Lord’s *Jiǔqì* (九炁) and *Wénchāng* (文昌宫):**
June, July

**The Palace of the Supreme Lord’s *Tiāndì* (天帝宫):**
August

**The Palace of the Supreme Lord’s *Dàdào* (大道宫):**
September, October

**The Palace of *Xuándū* (玄都宫) in the Intercalary Month (闰月):**
The Palace of the Supreme Lord’s Attendants and Marshals (大上侍中左右监诸将军宫)

**The Twenty-Eight Palaces of the *Cáo* (曹) and *Cháo* (朝) System:**
November 1 – *Cáo* (曹) of *Jiàn Yù* (建玉) and *Chìlíng* (赤灵宫)
November 2 – *Cáo* of *Tàisù* (太素) and *Tàiwéi* (太微宫)
November 3 – *Cáo* of *Tàiwéi* (太微) and *Běipíng* (北平宫)
November 4 – *Cáo* of *Dūzhèng* (都正) and *Tàiqīng Xiàgōng* (太清下宫)
November 5 – *Cáo* of *Zhèngyī* (正一) and *Tōngmíng* (通明宫)
November 6 – *Cáo* of *Xuányī* (玄一) and *Shàngmíng* (上明宫)
November 7 – *Cáo* of *Tàisù* (太素) and *Gāolíng* (高灵宫)
November 8 – *Cáo* of *Língjí* (灵集) and *Zǐwéi* (紫微宫)
November 9 – *Cáo* of *Yuánlíng* (元灵) and *Shìchūn* (侍春宫)
November 10 – *Cáo* of *Tàiqīng* (太清) and *Zǐlíng* (紫灵宫)
November 11 – *Cáo* of *Sānshuǐ* (三水) and *Sùnǚ* (素女宫)
November 12 – *Cáo* of *Sīlù* (司录) and *Jùyě* (巨野宫)
November 13 – *Cáo* of *Qīngxù* (清叙) and *Xīmíng* (西明宫)
November 14 – *Cáo* of *Xuánzhèng* (玄正) and *Shàngjiàng* (上降宫)
November 15 – *Cáo* of *Zhōngdū* (中都) and *Diǎnpíng* (典平宫)
November 16 – *Cáo* of *Sīfēi* (司非) and *Běifǔ* (北府宫)
November 17 – *Cáo* of *Sījiān* (司奸) and *Nánbó* (南伯宫)
November 18 – *Cáo* of *Tǒngbù* (统部) and *Dōngmíng* (东明宫)
November 19 – *Cáo* of *Tǒnglù* (统录) and *Xīlíng* (西灵宫)
November 20 – *Cáo* of *Jiānkǎo* (监考) and *Sīmìng* (司命宫)
November 21 – *Cáo* of *Jiānshì* (监司) and *Yángmíng* (阳明宫)
November 22 – *Cáo* of *Diǎnkǎo* (典考) and *Tàiyáng* (太阳宫)
November 23 – *Cáo* of *Sīguān* (司官) and *Shàoyáng* (少阳宫)
November 24 – *Cáo* of *Xuányuán* (玄元) and *Tàiyīn* (太阴宫)
November 25 – *Cáo* of *Tàixuán* (太玄) and *Shàoyīn* (少阴宫)
November 26 – *Cáo* of *Dūshì* (都司) and *Běichén* (北辰宫)
November 27 – *Cáo* of *Dūhòu* (都候) and *Tàibái* (太白宫)
November 28 – *Cáo* of *Zhíshǐ* (直使) and *Línmíng* (林明宫)
November 29 – *Cáo* of *Zhíshì* (直司) and *Yángmíng* (阳明宫)
November 30 – *Cáo* of *Diǎnkǎo* (典考) and *Qǐmíng* (启明宫)

**According to the *Jūdòng Wēi* (朱洞微) *Zhǐyào* (旨要):**
The above [palaces] are verified.

**The Six Sentences of the Jade Maiden (玉女):**
Each sentence shall have one Jade Maiden (玉女) on duty, without error.

**Jade Maidens of the *Tàixuán* (太玄) System:**
*Jiazi* (甲子) – Jade Maiden of *Tàixuán* (太玄)
*Jiāxū* (甲戌) – Jade Maiden of *Huángsù* (黄素)
*Jiāshēn* (甲申) – Jade Maiden of *Tàisù* (太素)
*Jiāchén* (甲辰) – Jade Maiden of *Bàijīng* (拜精)
*Jiāwǔ* (甲午) – Jade Maiden of *Jiànggōng* (绛宫)
*Jiāyín* (甲寅) – Jade Maiden of *Qīngyāo* (青腰)

**The Upper Three Divisions (上三部) are assigned to the Left *Língfēi* (灵飞) Jade Maiden, and the Lower Three Divisions (下三部) to the Right *Língfēi* (灵飞) Jade Maiden.**

**General Prayers for Confession (诸章通用谢罪):**
*"With the highest reverence, this lowly disciple [name], in deepest awe and trembling, prostrates and bows twice. I humbly address the Supreme Lord, the *Wújí Dàdào* (无极大道) of Ultimate Truth and Naturalness, beneath the Golden Gate (金阙). I am indeed a vulgar and unworthy being, a coarse and common mortal, yet by the grace of the Master and the favor of the Daoist lineage, I have been granted a place among those adorned with the Daoist cap and sash (簪裳之列).*

*I, [name], in deepest awe and trembling, prostrates and bows repeatedly. Reflecting upon my own inadequacies, I realize my learning is incomplete, my conduct flawed, and my transgressions numerous. I fear the punishment of Your divine censure and bear the heavy burden of my sins. Thus, I dare not fail to report—my humble petition is presented, though it falls short of Your celestial hearing. I, [name], am guilty of deathly crimes, deathly crimes!"*

*With the highest reverence, this lowly disciple [name], in deepest awe and trembling, prostrates and bows twice. I humbly address the Supreme Lord, the *Wújí Dàdào* (无极大道) of Ultimate Truth and Naturalness, beneath the Golden Gate (金阙). I, a vulgar and unworthy being, have presumptuously joined the Great Daoist Law (大法). My merits are as dust, my offenses as mountains. I am filled with shame and dread, my soul and body wandering in confusion.*

*I, [name], in deepest awe and trembling, guilty of deathly crimes, deathly crimes! Reflecting upon my own insignificance, I rely on past merits and, through divine grace, have encountered this wondrous transformation. I rejoice in Your boundless compassion, though I am unworthy of Your favor. Having now taken office in Your sacred ranks, I vow to fulfill my duties of salvation and guidance, though my nature is blind and dull. I pledge my sincere heart, seeking Your benevolent instruction and striving for righteousness, my conscience burdened day and night.*

*Given the circumstances, I dare not withhold this report. Though my petition falls short of Your celestial hearing, I submit it in utmost reverence."*

**After the Chapter (章后):**
*"This is done as a model of sincerity. The Supreme Lord’s teachings alone distinguish the truth. The *Yángōngzhāng* (言功章) states that the Supreme Lord’s assembly of all honored deities shall judge and accept sincere repentance. As a vulgar and unworthy being, I lack the purity to stand before You in direct petition, hence the phrase ‘through the two officials and the *Zhíshǐ* (直使) and others.’ These deities shall convey my words—this passage must not be altered or omitted."*

**With the highest reverence, I submit through:**
The two officials of the *Zhíshǐ* (直使) and *Zhèngyī* (正一) *Cáo* (曹),
the left and right officials of the *Shǐzhě* (使者),
the *Yīnyáng Shénjué* (阴阳神决) officers,
the *Kēchē* (科车) and *Chìfú* (赤符) officers,
the *Gāngfēng* (刚风) mounted officers,
the *Yìmǎ* (驿马) officers of the upper register,
the *Fēilóng* (飞龙) and *Shénlóng Tiānxiān* (神龙天仙),
the *Fēizhēn* (飞真) mounted officers,
and other officials—each two in number—who shall attend in order.*

**For my household, [name], who practices the *Dàocháng* (道场) of [specific Dao], I humbly request the Heavenly Official (天官君) to dispatch officers and soldiers. I submit a petition to the Three Heavens (三天), presenting one copy of this chapter, to be conveyed to the Supreme Lord’s [specific] Palace, [specific] *Cáo* (曹), and [specific] Jade Maiden (玉女). I await Your divine report. I, [name], in deepest awe and trembling, prostrates and bows twice. Below, I add my name and state my humble origin: [name], a disciple of [specific observatory], in [specific state/county].**

**Ancient Rituals and the *Tàiqīng Xiàn* (太清衔) are not to be used in [specific observatory’s] offerings or in the receipt of disciples.**

All petitions shall be uniformly made in strips of two *cùn* and four *fēn* in length, with characters and designs clearly delineated.

For the **Tàiqīng Xuányuān** (太清玄元), the **Wúshàng Sāntiān** (無上三天), the **Wújí Dàdào** (無極大道), the **Tàishàng Lǎojūn** (太上老君), the **Tàishàng Zhàngrén** (太上丈人), the **Tiāndìjūn** (天帝君), the **Tiāndì Zhàngrén** (天帝丈人), the **Jiǔlǎo Xiāndūjūn** (九老仙都君), the **Jiǔqì Zhàngrén** (九炁丈人), the **Bǎiqiānwànchóng Dàodào Qì** (百千萬重道炁), and the **Qiānèrbǎi Guānjūn** (千二百官君) of **Tàiqīng**—

To the **Yù Pìxià** (玉陛下, *Jade Sovereign*), for **Sānqīng** (三清) petitions, the length shall be one *cùn* and two *fēn*.

For the **Tàishàng Wúxíng Wúmíng** (太上無形無名), the **Xūwú Zìrán** (虛無自然), the **Wúshàng Sānzūn** (無上三尊), and the **Jīnquè Qībǎo** (金闕七寶)—

To the **Yù Pìxià** (玉陛下), the **year designation** shall be the **Tàisuì** (太歲) of the **Jiǎzǐ year**, month **shuò**, day **Jiǎzǐ**, at the **certain hour**, to be respectfully submitted within the *jiào* altar.

According to the *Xuāndū Lǜ* (玄都律), petitions are forbidden on **wùchén** (戊辰) and **wùxū** (戊戌) days.

**Xū** (戌) is the **Heavenly Gate** (天門), **chén** (辰) is the **Earthly Portal** (地戶).
**Xū** governs the **dog**, **chén** governs the **dragon**.
When **wù** (戊) aligns, the **Central Palace Earth Spirit** (中宫土神) presides.
On such days, the **Tàishàng Zhūjūn Zhàngrén** (太上諸君丈人) inspect the fate of all mortals—male and female—judging life, death, virtue, and vice.
The **dragon** traverses the **Five Peaks**, the **dog** patrols the **river crossings**, and the **Central Yellow Great Spirit** (中黃大神) guards the Heavenly Gate.
Transgressors shall have their **hun** and **pò** seized by the Great Spirit.

Should misfortune or death occur on **wùchén** or **wùxū**, it shall be deemed an offense.

「If one wishes to pray, simply purify the heart and sit upright, reflect upon past transgressions, and repent sincerely. The heavens shall know and grant mercy accordingly. Then, choosing an auspicious day, offer the petition—it shall never fail to be fulfilled.

**Consumption of Misfortune and Extension of Life Petition**
This is the work of Master Du, now recorded according to the *Xuānhuì Zhùhuà Zhāng* (宣慈助化章) within the Daoist Canon. On this very day, I humbly prostrate myself and present my words: though I am but a humble mortal, I have received the Dao’s transformation, my life depending on the **Supreme Polarity** (皇极), my **qi** descending from the **Nine Heavens** (九天). Endowed with divine essence and nature, I bear boundless grace.

Yet, though I stand in life, my conduct has strayed, my nature lost to indulgence. My blessings are shallow despite their depth, my sins manifold and unceasing. Should calamity strike, there shall be none to rescue me.

I dare to implore the **Dao**—the ultimate **Ren** (仁慈, benevolence)—who cherishes life and aids all beings. With a sincere heart and humble confession, my accumulated guilt may be pardoned.

Moreover, I fear that in my past lives and this present one, my actions and omissions—**Six Emotions** and **Ten Evils** (六情十恶)—have daily compounded my offenses. My **Three Actions** and **Ten Entanglements** (三业十缠) have only deepened my bonds, plunging me into the **netherworld’s snares** (网罟), from which I cannot free myself.

I also fear that across my **Nine Lives** and **Seven Ancestors** (九世七先), countless generations—**a hundred million ancestors** (亿曾万祖)—may have incurred transgressions, dragging my distant descendants into suffering.

Again, I fear that within my **destiny records** (命籍), the **Five Phases** (五行) may shift and alter, or that within the **Heavenly Decrees** (天度), the **Nine Luminaries** (九曜) may stray, bringing misfortune or disaster upon me.

Further, I fear that since my ancestors’ time, in my service as an official and governance of affairs, my rewards and punishments may have been unjust, causing the people to fall into wrongful suffering. The common folk may lament cruelty and oppression, their curses and invocations binding me to future calamities.

And I fear that within my dwelling, construction or labor involving **earth and wood** (土木) may disrupt the **qi**, violating the **celestial and terrestrial correspondences** (乖纬候之常). The divine and the **Spirits of Manifestation** (神明) may reproach me, thus inviting disaster.

Stricken with dread, I ponder endlessly. Should I cross a vast river, I know not how to escape.

Only with a single heart of devotion do I seek refuge in this petition, presenting it to the **Nine Heavens** for my own deliverance.

I humbly submit this petition to the **Southern Heavenly Officials** (南上君官), who command **one hundred and twenty spirits** (百二十人), to govern the **Pale Fruit Palace** (苍果宫), and beg them to open the **Heavenly Gate** (天门) for me, extending my life.

I also petition the **Life-Extending Officials** (寿命君官), who command **one hundred and twenty spirits**, to govern the **Peaceful Prosperity Palace** (安昌宫) and increase my fortune, prolong my years, and deliver me from misfortune and calamity.

Furthermore, I petition the **Southern Heavenly Officials of the Danran Order** (南昌丹秩君官), who command **one hundred and twenty spirits**, to govern the **Registry Palace** (列库宫) and restore my lost years, free me from the **register of the dead** (下死籍), absolve my sins and guilt in the **Yin Prefectures of the Northern Capital** (酆都之府), and inscribe my name in the **historical records** (历纪之中).

Additionally, I petition the **Officials of the Bright Hall** (明堂绛官君官), who command **one hundred and twenty spirits**, to govern the **City Qi Palace** (城炁宫) and increase my years of life, extending my destiny.

I also implore **Heavenly Official Tian Gong** (天公君) and **Wei Lang** (卫郎), who commands **thirty-nine thousand spirits** (三万九千人), to deliver me from suffering and calamity, guarding my vital **qi**.

*"Suffering"* refers to **crossing the calamities** (度厄). The scripture states that one crosses **three calamities and eight hardships** (三灾八难), yet many doubt this, often altering the text to their own detriment.

Next, I petition **Jade Calendar Lady Su Nu** (玉历素女), **one thousand two hundred spirits** (千二百人) clad in **red robes** (赤衣), to retrieve my **three hun** (三魂), restrain my **seven pò** (七魄), regulate my **Five Zang** and **Six Fu** (五藏六腑), pacify the **thirty-six thousand spirits** (三万六千神), and cleanse my afflictions, prolonging my life and extending my destiny.

I also petition **Official Zhou Yu** (周玉君官), who commands **one hundred and twenty spirits**, to govern the **Earthly Geography Palace** (地理宫) and summon **one hundred and twenty spirits of life and destiny** (百二十生炁神), clad in **red robes and celestial attire** (赤帧天衣), bearing the **sacred tablets** (仗节) to restrain my **three hun** and **seven pò**, ensuring they never leave my body. May they support my decline, guide me through calamity, and extend my life and destiny.

If my life is bound to **water**, the **Water Officials** (水官) shall release me.
If my life is bound to **earth**, the **Earth Officials** (地官) shall release me.
If my life is bound to **fire**, the **Fire Officials** (火官) shall save me.
If my life is bound to **wood**, the **Wood Spirits** (木神) shall protect me.
If my life is bound to **tombs and graves** (冢墓), they shall be opened and my fate extracted.
If my life is bound to **punishments and prisons** (刑狱), the chains shall be broken and I released.
If my life is bound to **detention**, the bonds shall be severed and I pardoned.
If my **life and fortune** (命禄) are near exhaustion, they shall be replenished.
If my **life and fortune** have already declined, they shall be restored and saved.

Even if no calamity strikes, if misfortune does not assail, and my destiny stretches far, let this be a sign of their efficacy. My gratitude is boundless, as with the **Supreme Dao** (太上云云).

**Petition for Ascension and Liberation**
On this day, I humbly present my words: I reflect upon my past blessings, now aligned with **auspicious clarity** (休明). The **Great Dao** flows, and the **Three Caverns** (三洞) teach. The **Ultimate True and Holy Sage** (至真大圣) rescues both heaven and mortals, allowing me, though humble, to revere the **True Law** (正法).

I dare to hope that the **Supreme Dao** (太上大道) and the **Heavenly Officials** (诸君丈人) shall extend their benevolent shade, blessing me across countless generations.

Yet I fear that my **hundred million ancestors** (亿曾万祖), both those who have passed and those who linger, along with my **family spirits and kin** (家亲眷属), whose souls I have recommended—whether in this life or through **infinite karmic causes and conditions** (积劫因缘)—have committed boundless sins, unpardoned and unredressed. They may not attain liberation, instead wandering the **Nine Abysses** (九幽), enduring endless nights of retribution. Some may be confined to the **Twenty-Four Prisons of Tai Mountain** (泰山岱宗二十四狱), the **Thirty-Seven Prisons of the Northern Capital** (北都罗酆三十七狱), or the **Great Prisons of the Eight Trigrams and Five Directions** (八卦五方九幽大狱). Others may dwell within the **Yin Prefectures of the Hundred Twenty Departments** (天地水府百二十司) across the **shades of state and county officials** (州县阴官), or in the **Netherworld’s Bureau of Darkness** (冥府之中), or beneath the **Yin and Yang Officials** (王官) in the **Bureaus of Water, Fire, Wind, and Knives** (阴阳水火风刀考官曹属).

Without the **Great Dao’s** (大道) mercy and **purgation of suffering** (亭毒之施), there is no way for them to ascend or be liberated.

Though I am unworthy as a descendant, I grieve for their torment. If one prays for another, as a husband for his wife or an elder for a younger, these two lines may be omitted, simply stating: *"I fear for [name]."*」

「If one wishes to employ this intention, one must first amend and correct it—do not use these exact words wholesale.

I fear that the departed [name] may be trapped in the **Yin Prefectures of the Night** (冥冥夜府), unable to see the light. Wandering through endless transmigrations, they endure suffering beyond measure. Thus, I dare to bare my heart and plead sincerely, turning toward the **Law’s Gate** (法门), relying on the **Great Compassion’s** (大慈) grace to seek and implore a decree. May their sins be absolved, and their spirits liberated, with my words filled with earnestness and genuine sorrow.

I humbly present this supplication to the **Celestial Bureaus** (天曹), beseeching the **Supreme Lord of the Dao** (太上老君), the **Supreme Elder** (太上丈人), the **Celestial Master** (天师), the **Female Master** (女师), the **Three Masters** (三师君), the **Five *Qi* Lords** (五炁君)—the **Five *Qi* Lords**, whose names are recorded as follows: *"The Five *Qi* Lords, including the **Lords of Generation and Rectification** (生炁、正炁君), are all without precedent in the scriptures."*—to carefully examine and grant favor.

I pray that the **Supreme Lord** (太上) may, through the **Dao’s *Qi* of Benevolence** (道炁下流), extend a **covering robe** (覆衣) to the spirits of my departed ancestors and relatives, all those recommended by me.

I further humbly request the **Great General of Redemption** (拔赎亡人魂魄大将军) and **Ten Million Soldier-Spirits** (兵士十万人) to unite and descend, commanding all those recommended by me who have passed away—including my own deceased, family kin, and distant relations—**all spirits** (一切魂灵)—to ascend from the **Prisons of the Eight Trigrams and Five Directions** (泰山岱宗二十四狱、北都罗酆三十七狱、八卦五方九幽大狱), the **Yin Prefectures of the Hundred Twenty Departments** (天地水府百二十司), the **shades of state and county officials** (州县阴官), and the **Netherworld’s Bureau of Darkness** (冥府之中), beneath the **Yin and Yang Officials** (王官) in the **Bureaus of Water, Fire, Wind, and Knives** (阴阳水火风刀考官曹属). May they escape the endless night of the **Nine Shades** (长夜九幽), ascending to the **Eight Heavenly Halls of Blessing** (八天福堂).

May they also liberate the spirits of men—**three souls and seven spirits** (三魂七魄)—and women—**three souls and fourteen spirits** (三魂十四魄)—from the **Bureaus of Judgment** (考谪), resolving grudges and enmities, entering the **Dao’s Palaces** (道宫) and finding peace in the **Land of Ease** (安乐之地). May they bless the living, ensuring prosperity for descendants, fortune in both life and death, tranquility for tombs, and no calamities arising. This is done in faith, relying solely on the **Supreme Lord’s** (太上) mercy.

---
**The Yellow Arrow Ritual of Universal Merit** (黄箓言功都章)
The ancient ritual for the **Yellow Arrow** (黄箓) concludes with this single supplication, encompassing both the **family and the state**, the **visible and invisible realms** (幽显), hence the term *"Universal Merit"* (都章).

I, the disciple [name], now bow my head and present these words in full: the **Supreme and Perfect Dao** (无上正法), the **Yellow Arrow Grand Ritual** (黄箓大斋), which transcends life and death. For my past and present selves, for my **body, speech, and mind’s deeds** (身口意业), may it benefit the **state’s longevity** (国祚) and all beings below (群生). May it safeguard the nation and bring peace to my family, ward off disasters and avert misfortunes, increase wealth and extend years, dissolve calamities and dispel afflictions, and liberate the **nine ancestors and seven generations** (九祖七先) and **all spirits** (一切魂爽). May it rescue both the living and the dead, and bless all realms—**visible and invisible** (幽显).

I bring **tenfold talismans of assurance** (十方镇信), my **native life-threads** (本命纹缯), oil lamps, incense, flowers, and all ritual offerings—**evidence of sincerity and proof** (证质丹诚)—and humbly present this petition.

Through my **practice of the Dao** (行道), I repent and offer my first gratitude. May all new and past sins be severed, and all suffering and guilt be erased. May the living and the dead alike be rescued, with my words sincere and heartfelt—**red as blood** (丹), **inverted in earnestness** (倒, 颠倒). The reasoning is clear.

I, the disciple [name], lead fellow **lecturing Daoists of the Law** (同法都讲道士), and according to the **Yellow Arrow Ritual of the Lower Element** (下元黄箓), the **Simplified Text for the Spirit of the Mysterious Dao** (简文灵仙科品), I solemnly establish the **ritual of the Mysterious Dao** (玄科之式) at [location]. Following the **celestial patterns and earthly forms** (法天象地), I dedicate the **golden dragon silks and colorful offerings** (金龙缯彩) brought by my family to **assure the ten directions** (镇十方), invoking the heavens and summoning the spirits to rescue the living and the dead, all striving together. With a **pure heart and tranquil mind** (刷心静念), I **bear witness with blood and bow in reverence** (涂炭稽颡), surrendering to the **Most True** (至真) to fulfill my wishes.

For **three days and three nights** (三日三夜), I perform the **Nine Daoic Practices** (九时行道) and **recite the scriptures nine times** (九遍诵经). Beginning at dawn on the [date], I ascend the platform and perform the rites, completing all **eighteen hours** (一十八时) of supplication. May my prayers be answered and my intentions realized, and I now declare the rites complete.

I dissolve the platform and disperse the offerings, casting the **golden dragon** (金龙) into the mountains and waters. I write a **red talisman** (丹书) with a brief inscription and present it to the **Spirit Platform** (灵坛). I kneel and prostrate myself, offering a **yellow-white talisman with red script** (黄素朱章) to the **Nine Heavens** (九天).

I humbly pray to the **Supreme Lord of the Limitless Dao** (太上无极大道元始天尊), the **Supreme Daoic Lord** (太上道君), the **Supreme Lord of the Dao** (太上老君), the **Supreme Elder** (太上丈人), the **Most High Mysterious Old One** (无上玄老), the **Ten-Directional Natural Treasures** (十方自然), the **Lord of the Numinous Treasure** (灵宝天尊), the **Already Enlightened Great Saints** (已得道大圣), the **Many True Ones** (众至真), the **Elders of All Heavens** (诸天丈人), the **Great Sovereign and Celestial Emperor** (太帝天帝), the **Great Lawmaster of the Mysterious Center** (玄中大法师), and the **Celestial Master Lord** (天师君). May they kindly hear my supplication and take pity on my sincere heart.

If the **Supreme Lord** (太上) grants favor and commands the **Five Old Celestial Deities** (五老上帝), the **Five Peaks and Four Seas True Immortals** (五岳真仙), the **Three Officials and Nine Prefectures of the Hundred Twenty Departments** (三官九府百二十曹), and the **Ten Realms of True Spirits** (十界真灵), may they liberate the spirits of my family’s **nine ancestors and seven generations** (九先七祖), both those with **affinity** (有缘) and those without (无缘), and all **grudge-bound spirits** (冤亲). May they all be granted liberation, escaping the **Nine Shades** (长夜九幽), ascending to the **Southern Palace** (南宫), where they may wear **official cap and sash** (冠带), their **dried bones flourishing** (枯骨生华), their transmigratory cycle complete (轮漏尽), and their rebirth into the **Gate of Blessings** (福门) fulfilled.

I pray to the **local deities** (所在土地), the **guardian spirits** (营卫尸形), and the **forms of the departed** (复神反旧), that they may reunite with their **shadows in the Netherworld** (景冥), as one.

May my family in past and present lives have all their sins cleansed and their grudges resolved. May they escape suffering and avert disasters, prolong life and safeguard their fate, and open the path of prosperity for both living and dead, with their descendants at peace.

I pray that the **Seven Luminaries** (七曜) may shine brightly, the **Two Principles** (二仪) endure forever, that **Yin and Yang** (阴阳) harmonize in order, the **Nine Granaries** (九谷) overflow with abundance, the nation grow rich and its people joyful, the world prosperous and tranquil, the **Six Extremes** (六合) peaceful, the **imperial lineage** (帝祚) extended, all **epidemics and poisons** (疫毒) eradicated, and **auspicious omens** (善瑞) ever increasing. May I attain **Great Auspiciousness** (元吉) and forever bear the **Dao’s grace** (道恩).

I now transfer the **heavenly armies of the ritual** (迁修斋所请天仙兵马、飞仙兵马、真人兵马、神人兵马、地仙兵马、日月星宿兵马、九宫五帝兵马、五岳四渎兵马、三河四海兵马), each numbering **nine hundred million cavalry** (九亿万骑). Including the **Supervising Officials of the Ritual** (监斋直事), the **Attendant Golden Boys** (侍香金童), the **Scattering-Flower Jade Girls** (散花玉女), the **Five Emperors’ Talismans** (五帝直符), the **Flying Dragon Messengers** (传言奏事飞龙骑吏), the **Daoist Officials within my body** (臣等身中内外真官), the **Numinous Treasure Officials** (灵宝官属), the **Guardian of the Household** (守宫), the **Residential Generals** (宅将军), the **local deities and territorial spirits** (此间土地里域真官), and the **Three Realms’ Divine Beings** (三界神祇)—all who oversee, guard, and command the ritual, and who have rendered service—may they all be **honored in splendid attire** (严装), accompanying my current talisman to the **Celestial Capital** (仙都), where they shall receive rewards and be listed among the **True Palaces of the Dao** (真宫). May they be **ranked according to their merit** (进品上仙), **promoted in status** (加爵进一作带秩), and **assigned their proper offices** (随品署职, 一作真高下等级), all elevated to the **Highest Daoic Honor** (崇达), as befits the **Most True** (太真).」

「Though my disciples’ learning and practice are yet incomplete, we now understand the **proper etiquette of reverence and humility** (學援未備，俯仰之格), as well as the **ritualized postures of bowing and kneeling in the Daoist tradition** (教中有俯仰節奏之格), and we **specialize in the correct rites of morning obeisance** (專明朝謁拜跪之儀).

In matters of **advancement, retreat, or transgression of Daoic precepts** (進止犯科), we have failed to observe the proper ritual forms (不合儀式). We fear that the **Four Celestial Bureaus** (四司) may **disapprove** (所斜), and the **Five Emperors** (五帝) may **lay blame** (所執), for our **countless offenses and myriad errors** (千愆萬過). We **pray for Your Most High Grace to pardon and forgive** (乞蒙赦宥), and **for our humble ignorance to be spared punishment** (哀原未悟，不見罪罚).

My disciples’ **Five Vital Daoic Officials within our bodies** (臣等身中五體真官) have now **fulfilled their duties** (受功事訖), and each **returns to their respective palaces** (各還宮府).

May this allow my disciples to **attain the Dao through study** (學道得道), **seek the True and find it** (求真得真), and **ascend as Daoic Immortals forevermore** (一作仙永為真人). *In some ancient rites, this passage is omitted, and instead the phrase "long-lasting as the Three Lights and Seven Luminaries"** (古儀無此句與三光七曜五炁長存) is included, **as a testament to our sincerity and faith** (以為效信). We **solemnly entrust ourselves to the Most High’s boundless compassion** (恩惟太上眾真分別雲雲).

In the **establishment of the boundless Yellow Arrow Talismanic Rite for the House of [Name]** (操臣所為某家修設無量下元黃箓大斋), we have **conducted a three-day, four-night fast** (三日四夜), **completing our supplications openly** (露請事竟). Now, having **dissolved the ritual platform** (解壇), we **seek transfer to our Daoic offices** (遷職), **restoring our positions among the Celestial Hierarchies** (復諸天位), and **reaffirming our merit and virtue** (重明功德). We **present a single Yellow Silk Talisman with Red Characters** (進拜黃素朱章一通) to **ascend to the Three Celestial Tribunals** (上詣三天曹雲雲).

**For the newly added "Prayer for National Auspices" (為國祈祥章新添),** we **now prostrate ourselves in obeisance** (即日稽首列詞), **humbly awaiting Your Most High Response** (伏聞). We have **received the omen of the Luo River Diagram** (河圖已兆), and **the grand patterns of the Daoic classics are now manifest** (克彰經緯之文);」

«Once the heart’s diagram is complete, it conveys the **virtue/power (德)** of attaining divine clarity (神明).
All are illuminated by the **Dao/Way (道)** of the sages, reaching the utmost harmony of human relationships (彝伦).
How much more so the **august Celestial Sovereign (皇天)**, who blesses the realm below, and the **rulers (君师)** whom He has established—
They should be revered by the people as the **posterity (戴后)** united with the sun and moon.
From the **Poetry of the *Tianbao* era (天保之诗)**, one knows to repay above with below;
To the **extreme foundations of the *Hongfan* (洪范)**, blessings are bestowed upon the people.

In this age of **clarity and abundance (清裕)**, it is as if we have returned to the **primordial chaos (鸿荒)**.
With deep reflection, the **fasting master (斋主)**, [Name], though unaware of daily sustenance (日用),
Who could dare to **seek celestial favor (天休)** in reply?
Together we cherish the **loyalty of safeguarding the state (卫祉之忠)**,
And humbly offer the **prayers of the *Fengren* (封人)**.

Now, with **reverent devotion, we prepare the sacred offerings (恭修宝供)**,
And **carefully follow the Daoic cycles (谨按冲科)**.
We **invoke the lofty vault of heaven (请命高穹)**,
And **return to the Great Dao/Way (归心大道)**.
With **respectful supplication, we seek the Talisman and Tablet (敬求章表)**,
And **present them to the Three Celestial Tribunals (上奏三天)**.

Though I am but a **lowly mortal (凡微)**,
I have **gained access to the esoteric mysteries (参秘奥)**.
**Establishing merit as the foundation (立功为本)**,
I place the **nation’s welfare above all (为国居先)**.
With **deepest humility, I kneel before the earth (伏地)**,
And **proffer this Yellow Silk Talisman with Red Characters (拜奏黄素朱章一通)**,
To **submit to the Celestial Hierarchies (上闻天曹)**.
I **boldly implore the Most High Dao/Way of the **Wujie Great Dao (无极大道)**, the **Yuan Shi Tian Zun (元始天尊)**,
The **Yucheng Yuan Huang Dao Jun (玉宸元皇道君)**,
The **Laojun Gun Yuan Shang (老君棍元上)**,
The **Emperor of Virtue (德皇帝)**,
The **Tian Ren (丈人)**,
The **Celestial Master (天师)**,
The **Female Master (女师)**,
And the **Three Masters (三师)**,
Along with the **Five *Qi* Lords (五炁君)**,
To **pause and reflect (留神平省)** upon the **petition (章书)** I have presented,
And **bestow it with the *Qi* of the Dao (流以道炁衣覆)**.
The **character for *Qi* (炁)** is pronounced with a **departing tone (去声)**.
The **scripture says (传云)**: *"The Great Dao/Way clothes and covers all things (大道衣被万物)."*
May **divine response (真灵)** be **felt and granted (感降)**.»

I **respectfully petition** the Celestial Hierarchies for:
- **One Star Lord (营星君)** and **one hundred twenty officials and soldiers (官将)**, to govern the **Luo River Inverted Palace (洛逆宫)**, and **pursue and capture malefactors (逐捕群凶)** to **bring peace to the people (安万姓)**.

- **Ten thousand Day-Moon Heavenly Soldiers (日月天兵)**, clad in **red headbands and scarlet robes (衣赤帻红衣)**, to **regulate yin and yang (主理阴阳)** and **repel bandits and thieves (辟斥寇盗)**.

- **One thousand two hundred Day-Male Lords (日男君)**, clad in **white robes (衣白衣)**, to **subdue rebellious souls (桔伏逆人)** and **transform their hearts to align with the Dao (革心顺化)**.

- **One Lord of the People (万姓君)** and **one hundred ten officials (官将)**, to govern the **Harmonious Mountain Palace (和山宫)**, and **subdue those whose hearts and intentions are corrupt (伏天下之人，心腹不正、为恶逆者)**.

- **One Eastern and Western Great White Lord (东西太白君)** with **one hundred twenty officials (官将)**, to govern the **Nine-Heaven Primordial Palace (九天乾宫)**, and **suppress deceit and evil (主制伏奸恶)**, as well as those who **plot madness and treachery (好为狂孽谋议者)**.

- **Twenty thousand soldiers from the Human Arsenal (人库兵士)**, **ten thousand soldiers under the Shaking-Heaven-Moving-Earth Lord (摇天动地君)**, and **ten thousand soldiers under the Supreme Nine-*Qi* Lord (无上九炁君)**, to **restrain and subdue the wicked (摄制奸凶)**, **abandon rebellion and embrace order (舍逆从顺)**, and **turn toward the sovereign’s transformation (宾向王化)**, **prostrate before the court (稽首阙庭)**, **forever lay down arms (永释戈矛)**, and **cease border conflicts (息边患)**.

I **humbly pray** that Your **august person (圣躬)** may be **harmonious and unobstructed (和畅)**, Your **divine wisdom (睿算)** **prolonged and boundless (绵长)**, Your **virtue surpassing that of Tang and Yu (盛德迈於唐虞)**, Your **divine transformation exceeding that of Wen and Wu (神化高於文武)**, Your **sacred lineage descending from the Silver River (衍灵源於银汉)**, and Your **grand foundation rooted in the Jade Capital (隆大本於玉京)**. May Your **glory flourish eternally (炽而昌)**, Your **years be long and Your people prosperous (曰寿而富)**. May all **officials within and without (中外官僚)** **cherish loyalty, integrity, and rectitude (怀忠良正直之心)**, so that **rains and winds may be timely (风雨时而)**, **harvests abundant (百谷丰登)**, **plagues and epidemics dissipate (灾疠消)**, and **the people thrive in peace (万民康乂)**. May this **quickly harmonize with the grand design (早谐恢拓)** and **permanently secure prosperity (永保升平)**, as a **verifiable testament to Your grace (以为效信)**.

---
**Divorce and Litigation Petition (分解冢讼章)**
**Dimensions:** Three *zhang* six *chi* (三丈六尺), **seventeen characters per line (每行十七字)**.
**Formatting Note:** Leave **empty spaces (下已空字数)** for later adjustment—**add or subtract characters as needed (临时随宜加减)** to complete **seventeen characters per line (足成十七字)**, ensuring the **entire text remains unaltered in structure (免有迁动全本)**.

**Offerings (章信):**
- **Yellow-white silk (黄素)** – **thirty-six *zhang* (三十六尺)**
- **Purple brocade (紫罗命缯)** – **thirty-six *zhang* (三十六尺)**
- **Cinnabar (丹砂)** – **one *liang* (一两)**
- **Silver dagger (银刀)** – **one, five *cun* long (一口长五寸)**
- **Sacred coins (命钱)** – **three *guan* six hundred *wen* (三贯六百文)**
- **Rice tribute (禄米)** – **twelve *sheng* (一十二升)**
- **Sophora japonica paper (槐黄纸)** – **one hundred twenty sheets (百二十张)**
- **Superior ink (上色笔)** – **one pair (一对)**
- **Superior inkstick (上色墨)** – **one (一笏)**
