I **respectfully inform the Celestial Hierarchies and Netherworld Officials (启天曹地府冥司众官)** that, according to the **orthodox Daoist precepts (正一明科)** and **Celestial Master rituals (天师仪典)**, the **Great Dao/Way extends its laws (大道垂法)** to **rescue and protect all living beings (济护群生)**. The **one thousand two hundred officials’ petitions (千二百官章)** **salvage both the living and the dead (拯度存殁)**, and the **ten directions of sacred beings (十方众圣)** **all bear witness (咸所证知)**.

Now, **Your disciple (弟子某)**, with **sincere and earnest words (所陈词悃)**, **dares to seek Your compassion (欲冒哀怜)**.

I **fear that since ancient times (窃虑上世以来)**, the **departed and the recently deceased (先亡后逝)** have **lodged grievances against the living (诉讼生人)** within the **Netherworld offices (阴官冥府)** and **ghostly realms (神趣鬼趣)**. These include:
- **Drowning deaths (溺死之讼)**, where the **body sinks in water (沉沦水符)**, **clinging to dampness (尸形沾湿)**.
- **Burning deaths (烧死之讼)**, where **hair and skin are scorched (发肤焦灼)**, **flesh peeled away (皮肉剥烂)**.
- **Wounding deaths (伤死之讼)**, where **the body is mutilated (身形残毁)**, **bloodied and lingering (流连疮血)**.
- **Hanging deaths (绞死之讼)**, where **the noose is tight (绳约紧急)**, **breath choked (气息壅闭)**.
- **Prison deaths (狱死之讼)**, where **chains bind (械锁攀挛)**, **escape impossible (不得解脱)**.
- **Imprisonment deaths (囚死之讼)**, where **the dungeon is oppressive (囹圄幽严)**, **justice stifled (道理不畅)**.
- **Exile deaths (徒系死之讼)**, where **shackles weigh heavy (枷杻在身)**, **labor cruel (谪役苦剧)**.
- **Fracture and fall deaths (折伤堕落死之讼)**, where **bones are shattered (筋骨摧碎)**.
- **Beating deaths (棒杖死之讼)**, where **the body bears torture (身被考掠)**.

**Death by Poison (毒药死之讼)**, where the intestines and stomach rot away (肠胃溃烂).

**Death by Tiger or Wolf (被虎狼啮死之讼)**, where flesh is devoured (肌肤啖食).

**Death in Childbirth (产乳死之讼)**, where the womb splits and blood rages (肠裂腥躁).

**Suicide by Hanging (自缢死之讼)**, where officials or private forces drove them (官私所逼).

**Suicide by Beheading (自刎死之讼)**, where their deeds were exposed (所为败露).

**Death from Fetal Harm (损胎死之讼)**, where they never saw the light (未睹光明).

**Murdered Death (被杀死之讼)**, where ancient grudges festered (宿有冤对).

**Death by Lightning Strike (雷霆震击死之讼)**, where they offended the divine (犯忤神明).

**Death by Demon Possession (精魅所惑之讼)**, where the mind was unrighteous (心思不正).

**Death by Robbery (强盗劫掠死之讼)**, where past debts remained unpaid (宿债未偿).

**Death from Prolonged Illness (久病不痊死之讼)**, where stagnation and suffering dragged on (沈滞困剧).

**Death from Epidemic (疫疠传染死之讼)**, where kin abandoned them, and without aid, they perished (亲戚不往，无人救疗卒死).

**Death from Sudden Illness (不通医治之讼)**, where fate struck abruptly (大限忽至).

**Death by Starvation (饥饿死之讼)**, where the stomach was hollow (胃腑空虚).

**Death by Cold (寒冻死之讼)**, where shivering froze the body (战栗冰冻).

**Death by Heat and Thirst (热渴死之讼)**, where flames scorched the flesh (炎赫焦烂).

**Death by Nightmare (魇死之讼)**, where terror seized the spirit, and malevolent ghosts subdued them (精神怖悸，邪鬼制伏).

**Death from Malaria (疟病死之讼)**, where cold and heat reversed (寒热颠倒).

**Death from Sudden Sickness (中恶死之讼)**, where violent illness struck swift, and grievances went unvoiced (暴病卒急，意不得伸).

**Death from Cholera (霍乱死之讼)**, where hunger, labor, and disrupted *honor-wei* systems overwhelmed (饥饱劳役，荣卫翻错).

**Death from Abscess (痈疽死之讼)**, where skin festered with pus and blood, and organs rotted (皮肤脓血，脏腑溃烂).

**Death from Dropsy (浮肿死之讼)**, where *qi* and vessels stagnated, and the body swelled (气脉瘨疰，身体胖胀).

**Death by Crushing (压死之讼)**, where bones were ground to ruin (筋骨摩溃).

**Death from Untreated Illness (疾病不救死之讼)**, where no skilled physician came (不遇良医).

**Death by Old Age (老死之讼)**, where bones grew weary (筋骨疲顿).

**Death in Youth (少亡之讼)**, where life’s purpose remained unfulfilled (年志未成).

**Death in Solitude (孤死之讼)**, where youth lacked shelter (幼无荫覆).

**Death Alone (独死之讼)**, where age left no support (老无依托).

**Death as a Widower (鳏死之讼)**, where loneliness was unbearable (只形难处).

**Death as a Widow (寡死之讼)**, where separation brought sorrow (离别悲孀).

**Death Away from Home (客死之讼)**, where homesickness tore at them (怀乡隔越).

**Death Exposed to the Elements (露死之讼)**, where the body had no covering (形无覆盖).

**Death Without a Coffin (死无棺椁之讼)**, where the corpse mingled with the earth (体亲土壤).

**Unburied Corpse (尸骸不埋之讼)**, where they were not laid to rest among the reeds (不归蒿里).

**Scattered Remains (骸骨不合之讼)**, where limbs were torn asunder (肢节分张).

**Corpse Mutilated by Beasts (鸟兽残啄之讼)**, where flesh was forever lost (永失肌肤).

**Cremation (焚尸之讼)**, seeking restoration.

**Waterlogged Bones (渍骨之讼)**, seeking dry elevation.

**Crushed by Wheels or Hooves (车马践轹之讼)**, where harm differed from others (受患害而与人异).

**Defiled Graves (凿掘秽污之讼)**, seeking relocation.

**Burial Repairs (已葬之讼)**, seeking mending.

**Unburied (未葬之讼)**, seeking a grave.

**Burial in the Wrong Plot (葬非本墓之讼)**, seeking proper grounds.

**Burial Violating Taboos (葬犯禁忌之讼)**, seeking absolution.

**Unstable Burial (葬不稳便之讼)**, seeking relocation.

**Graves in Harmful *Qi* (地气冲激高下四方之讼)**, where the site shifted chaotically (处所更相转动).

**Disputes Among Seven Generations (七祖父母中外六亲九族互相牵引之讼)**, where the living defied familial bonds (生人违背恩纪).

**Child Reared but Uncared For (育子不养之讼)**, where nature’s nurture was denied (天性忍害，不得生成).

**Slavery for Offspring (有男女不举没为奴婢之讼)**, where dignity was crushed (屈抑).

**Disputes Over Same-Clan Marriage (同姓之讼)**, where lineage branches scattered and kin grew distant (宗枝散蔓，递相疏隔).

**Disputes Over Inter-Clan Marriage (异姓之讼)**, where vows were broken mid-course (结托婚姻，中途背义).

**Homelessness (无宅之讼)**, where there was nowhere to return (靡有所归).

**Housing in Disrepair (有宅之讼)**, seeking repairs (补葺).

**Having Heirs but No Filial Care (有后之讼)**, where gratitude was absent (无恩养).

**No Heirs (无后之讼)**, where ancestral rites ended (绝祭祀).

**Wrongful Accusations (责怒之讼)**, where others encroached (人侵欺).

**Excessive Grief (悲伤之讼)**, where hardship and injustice piled high (多阨枉).

**Sudden, Unspoken Death (奄忽之讼)**, where no words could be left (不获词).

**Death with Favoritism (有宠爱之讼)**, where affection lingered unresolved (慕恋不断).

**Death with Enmity Unresolved (有冤雠之讼)**, where power silenced their voice (恃势难言).

**Feuds Unresolved (争伐之讼)**, where grudges festered (衔恨不了).

**Unclear Verdict in Murder Cases (杀活之讼)**, where justice was obscured (所报不明).

**Shame and Regret (惭负之讼)**, where the heart was burdened (心有所慊).

**Broken Vows (约誓之讼)**, where love endured beyond life (恩爱不绝).

**Curses (咒诅之讼)**, where rage fueled oaths (忿怒盟誓).

**Unjust Condemnation (枉滥之讼)**, where truth remained buried (情理不雪).

**Posthumous Slander (死后受诂之讼)**, where the living must testify (要生人作证).

**Posthumous Punishment (受考责之讼)**, where the living must stand in (要生人充替).

**Posthumous Imprisonment (受徒系之讼)**, where the living must redeem (要见存拔赎).

**Posthumous Exile (受谪役之讼)**, where the living must intervene (要生人求救).

**Posthumous Punishment in the Twenty-Four or Thirty-Seven Hells (受二十四狱、三十七狱罪报之讼)**, where the living must intervene to free (要生人追拔).

**Seeking Pardon (求宽赦之讼)**, where the living must earn merit (要生人功德).

All such grievances, though broadly eighty-one in number, branch into myriad forms—hundreds, thousands, millions.

Further, those who lived in transgression and died under punishment—boiled in water, scorched by fire, sliced by wind-knives, struck by thunder, burdened with stones, crushed in mountains, drowned in rivers, or sealed in caves—such fates number in the hundreds, thousands, millions.

All stem from death’s aftermath, where the dead drag descendants into disputes, forcing them to confront one another.

Again, when the underworld conceals the guilty, and spectral lawsuits drag on, if timing is unripe, misfortune descends—unbearable sorrow, bitter words, curses hurled at heaven and earth, defiling the divine—all trace to these lawsuits.

Or, should one’s life be vile, their sins countless, violating every statute and prohibition, all enter the ledger of judgment.

Centuries, half-centuries, decades, years, months, days, and moments—
all accumulate in judgment, their sins converging.
After death, the reckoning does not cease, its torment clinging, piling upon itself.

From past lives onward, the dead before and after—
should any transgress these precepts,
the day of reckoning arrives, unbearable in its weight,
summoning ghosts and gods, blaming heaven and earth,
bringing calamity from above and below,
yet never resolving.

Or, ruling over the people with perverse justice—
falsely accusing the innocent, killing for gain,
extorting the destitute, accepting bribes,
abusing authority for private gain,
cruel and violent, severing familial bonds,
plundering lineage and kin,
shattering harmony, severing love—

Or trusting deceitful flatterers,
slandering kin, oppressing inferiors,
nurturing grudges and malice,
invoking curses through sorcery and witchcraft,
harassing the virtuous, seizing souls,
[□] suppressing spirits—

Or excavating earth, violating taboos,
damaging ancestral halls and temples,
defiling divine traces,
drawing the wrath of true deities.

Such offenses, when transformed into lawsuits,
are boundless in number.

Yet further, fearing that my seven generations of ancestors
have accumulated hidden sins and overt transgressions,
living crimes and posthumous guilt,
concealed enmities and accumulated faults,
without virtue or kindness,
unfilial and unrighteous, deceitful and false—
acts no human should commit—

Unendurable by heaven and earth, abhorred by both gods and men,
when death comes, all three officials exact retribution,
guilt begetting guilt, binding across lifetimes,
never ceasing, souls restless, torment unbearable,
chaotically appealing to ghostly magistrates,
begging living kin to bear their suffering in place.

Though the underworld’s justice is clear,
it is not without corruption—
sometimes heeding ghostly pleas,
issuing summons for confrontation,
causing me to endure years of disaster,
decades of decline,
dreaming of omens and portents,
wealth depleted, endeavors failing,
petitions unanswered, supplicating officials,
dividing ancestral lawsuits,
sealing tomb registers with curses,
rescuing lost souls,
freeing wronged spirits from torment.

I humbly invoke the Great Dao,
whose saintly power is unfathomable,
yet through human error, paths diverge and stray.
Thus, with sincere devotion, I earnestly pray,
following the rites, offering in reverence:
yellow silk, cinnabar, grain, paper, ink, a writing knife, patterned fabrics,
to petition the Celestial Officials,
seeking absolution for myself.

I solemnly present a *bàishàng kǒuchāng* (supplication scroll) and beseech
the Ten-Directional Saints of the Great Dao’s Supreme Authority
to examine my disciple’s case—
to dissolve the ancestral lawsuits of the dead before and after,
extinguishing the accumulated torment,
separating the paths of the living and dead,
ensuring eternal estrangement.

I pray that the Celestial Official, along with his attendants and soldiers,
each overseeing their domain,
may subdue the tomb’s malevolent *qi*,
dispel the accumulated guilt,
descend spirits to suppress calamity,
eradicating all disasters.

Further, at the domains of *Yīngdū*, *Tàishān*, the rivers and seas, and the hills,
where exiled spirits labor,
before the Three Officials and Nine Departments,
each according to their pardons and records,
I command their release and absolution.

In accordance with the *Thousand-Two-Hundred Officials Chapter* of the Supreme One,
and the methods taught by the *Zhēngyī Zhēnrén* (Authentic Immortal of Unity)
to *Wèi Furen* (Lady Wei of Nanyue) for healing and exorcism,
I petition the Five *Tàixuān* Lords, each with one hundred twenty officers,
to govern the *Tàiqīng* Palace.

I also petition the Five *Dūhóu* Lords, each with one hundred twenty officers,
to govern the *Tàiqīng* Palace.

I further petition the Auxiliary General and his officers,
wielding the *Tàixuān* True Talismans,
to seize and dissolve the accumulated tomb curses,
the entangled lawsuits of the wronged dead,
including the underworld officials,
and command them to cease their accusations against my disciple—
for those of the *Jiǎo* clan, invoking the *Jùmáng* deity;
for those of the *Zhēng* clan, invoking the *Zhùróng* deity;
for those of the *Shāng* clan, invoking the two *Lùshōu* deities;
for those of the *Yǔ* clan, invoking the *Xuánmíng* deity;
for those of the *Gōng* clan, invoking the *Jùchén Hòutǔ* deity—
as well as the *Qiūchéng*, *Mùbó*, the *Diàixià Èrqiānshí* *Cānglín Jūn*,
the *Wǔyí Wáng*, the Left and Right *Zǒnghóu*,
the *Dìzhōng Sìxiá*, the *Mùqīng Yòuzhí*,
the *Háolǐ* elders, and all local domain lords—
to sever all tomb-related lawsuits against my disciple,
undoing the accumulated curses.

Should my seven generations of ancestors—
parents, uncles, brothers, collateral kin—
or any ancestral tombs where offenses occurred,
be marked by the *shíèr yuè jiàn* (twelfth-month taboo),
the *Pòwáng Shuāimù* (tomb-opening calamity),
the Eight Generals and Six Oppositions,
or violations of prohibitions—
where alignment is reversed, auxiliary positions unclear,
left and right disordered, male and female seats misplaced—
if these bring misfortune, endless depletion,
or harm descendants—
I pray for resolution, harmony restored,
life and death reconciled, all finding peace.

I further petition one *Tàixuān* Lord with one hundred twenty officers
to govern the *Nǚqú* Palace,
and one *Jiǔdì* Lord with one hundred twenty officers
to govern the *Dìlǐ* Palace,
uniting their forces below to address
my disciple’s transgressions in burial and interment,
the *shíèr yuè jiàn* and *Pòwáng* depletion,
as well as the twelve soil-tomb lawsuits—
all to be utterly extinguished.

I also petition the Five *Dūxīng* Lords, each with one hundred twenty officers,
to govern the *Qīnggài* Palace,
the Five *Zhūyāng* Lords, each with one hundred twenty officers,
to govern the *Cāngmíng* Palace,
and the Five *Tàibái Zhōngchén Míngxīng* Lords, each with one hundred twenty officers,
uniting their forces below to address
my disciple’s seven generations of ancestors—
the dead before and after, their stellar connections unbroken,
stars of the dead still binding,
the twelve celestial punishments,
retrograde killings, and obstructed deaths—
all to be removed, their influence halted, calamities erased.

Again, I petition the **Chìtiān Cāngqì** Lords—five in number, each with one hundred twenty officers—to drive away and repel the spirits of close and distant kin alike, as well as those of unrelated litigants and all malevolent ghosts who bring accusation and arrest.

I also petition the **Wúshàng Gāocāng** Lords—five in number, with ten million soldiers—to govern the spirits of the five tombs, to halt the comings and goings of the deceased, and to cure diseases and afflictions that torment the living.

I further petition the **Sìmíng** Lords, with one hundred twenty officers each, to disperse the ghosts of those who have passed away in litigation, as well as the errant *qì*, and to bring peace to those who are restless and unsettled.

I also petition the **Tiānchāng** Lords, clad in yellow robes, with ten million soldiers, to govern the hundred twenty calamities and spirits within my disciple’s household, as well as those from within and without who bring the twelve monthly punishments and killings.

I petition the **Shōushén Shàngmíng** Lords, with one hundred twenty officers each, to govern the restless and unsettled, the chaotic nightmares, and the wandering souls that do not abide.

I also petition the **Gàitiān Dàjiāngjūn**—one in number, with ten million soldiers—to clear away the lingering *qì* of my disciple’s ancestors, to sever the ghosts who bring lawsuits, to repel death and birth, and to repel calamities while inviting blessings.

I further petition the **Tàibái** Lords—ten million in number, with officials and inspectors, and the *Kàoduì Shājiān* Lords, each with their respective ranks numbering in the hundreds of thousands and millions—to unite and descend below, guarding and protecting my disciple’s body and household, severing the records of the dead, and halting the registration of life names. Let them also cut off the influence of the deceased from within and without, and the malevolent, impure *qì* of those who have died. May they command the dispersal of all spirits of calamity, preventing them from lurking, spying, or bringing further accusations and arrests. If the lingering *qì* of the dead assume forms or shadows, lead ghostly armies, or conspire to harass the deceased, thereby causing them to drag down the household, they shall be dealt with according to the *Nǚqīng Xuānmíng* ordinance, to be captured, governed, and utterly extinguished.

I also petition the **Bázhú Wángrén Húnpò** Lords—one in number, with ten million soldiers—to rescue and redeem the spirits of my disciple’s household. May they relocate and extract the souls of those recommended by my disciple: men with three souls and seven spirits, women with three souls and fourteen spirits. May they dissolve the litigations, release grudges and resentments, and guide them into the Daoist halls, to lands of peace and ease.

I humbly beseech the honored celestial officials, soldiers, and clerks to act according to their duties, and thus for my disciple to be relieved of the suffering of the deceased, to heal all afflictions, to cure all troublesome illnesses, and to attain perfect safety. May they ensure that no more lawsuits arise, that all calamities and registrations cease, and that the spirits of those who died before their time, the central and external kin, unrelated relatives, servants, and maids—who perished violently, unjustly, or without proper burial, or who had no descendants—all rest quietly and cease to bring harm.

For all the preceding eighty-one matters of litigation, as well as the myriad forms of calamities, registrations, and arrests, may they all be pacified and cease to act, bringing no further depletion or harm. If any should still harbor resentment, spy on opportunities, or incite calamities, they shall be utterly captured and repelled, ensuring they never rise again.

After this petition, I pray that the spirits of my disciple’s household—those who died before their time and those who passed away naturally, as well as the seven generations of ancestors—be granted pardon, with their souls ascending to the Three Heavens and their tombs and graves brought to peace. May all litigations be resolved, and may my disciple’s household be filled with blessings in future generations, with descendants prospering, virtuous officials ascending in rank, scholarly achievements fulfilled, and all endeavors meeting with success. May their lifespan be extended, calamities and decline avoided, the aged grow young, the young remain youthful, and their dreams be true and serene. May their homes be free from disturbances, all illnesses cured, and the spirits of the nine generations and seven ancestors ascend to the celestial halls, with all wandering souls swiftly released. This shall serve as proof of their efficacy, and the grace is from the **Tàishàng** alone.

As for the actions taken for my disciple’s household—erecting a certain Daoist altar and petitioning the celestial officials—they have been submitted to the Three Heavens. This petition is comprehensive in safeguarding and extracting the spirits, leaving nothing omitted.

Those who wish to pray should not need to submit another petition for relocation and extraction, lest it be deemed irreverent. The four preceding petitions have been composed according to ancient rituals and verified with the *Guānhào Jīng*. The officials and their duties are all correctly aligned, with no errors.

**Shìhuǒ Zhāng**—My disciple and all household members now kneel and present their words.

We humbly reflect that, though we are of humble origins, we have long benefited from the Dao’s teachings. Our lives have been fraught with suffering, and our sins have accumulated greatly. We fear that within the state and counties, the villages and neighborhoods, and wherever we dwell, fire disasters may arise unchecked. In our anxiety, there is no means to avert or appease them.

We have heard that the **Zhèngyī Dàfǎ** and the **Tiānshī Bǎozhāng** can rescue and save all living beings, dispel misfortunes, and avert calamities such as those brought by heaven—diseases, epidemics, floods, fires, droughts, and locusts. The sacred power can dispel and protect the myriad people, while the **Língxiān** can rescue and eliminate demons and malevolent forces.

Thus, we dare to devote our hearts wholeheartedly, relying on the Great Dao above, and humbly beseech its protection. We, the disciples, are deeply moved by this grace and submit this petition to the celestial tribunal, praying to the **Tàishàng Lǎojūn**, **Tàishàng Zhàngrén**, **Tiānshī**, **Nǚshī**, and the **Sānshī** Lords, as well as the Five *Qì* Lords, to heed our words and transmit this petition to the highest authority. We pray that the Dao’s *qì* flow downward, covering and shielding my disciple’s household, washing away all illnesses and misfortunes, and extending their years and blessings.

I humbly petition the **Xīnshàng Xuānmíng** Lords—one in number, with one hundred twenty officers—to protect my disciple’s household from the fire spirits of the four directions and eight winds, which penetrate a thousand feet into the earth, bringing no strange apparitions. May they extinguish all malevolent influences and safeguard the state and counties, as well as all places where my disciple resides, ensuring no disasters or epidemics intrude.

I also petition the **Běifāng Rénjǐ Shuǐguān**, **Hài Zǐ Jiānglì**, **Hébó Shuǐyuán**, **Lóngwáng Guānshǔ**, **Xuánwǔ Jiāngjūn**, and the **Wèibīng Jiānglì**—with soldiers numbering in the hundreds of thousands and millions—to unite and descend below, capturing the fire spirits such as **Sòng Wújì** and delivering them to the **Rénjǐ Shuǐ** authorities. May they swear to restrain these spirits, ensuring that within the state and counties, as well as my disciple’s household, no fire disasters arise, no strange apparitions appear, and the realm remains peaceful while the villages are tranquil. May the people be secure, their homes prosperous and auspicious, all endeavors successful, and their prayers answered.

**Translation:**

**File: Wénchāng Zhāng**
But the *jìnshì* [certain names], today prostrate and humbly present their petition.

In deepest reflection, we were born as offspring of officials, raised in the mundane world, yet by fortune and fate encountered the Dao’s transformation—granted by Heaven and Earth. Our master taught us the *Xún* [Confucian teachings] and *Shī* [classics], guiding us to be scholars and gentlemen. Yet the Five Constants of virtue were neglected in practice, and the Three Bonds of propriety were often transgressed. Our merits are as light as a hair’s tip, while our faults weigh like mountains; day after day, month after month, our flaws accumulate without purification. Like ice over deep waters, we tremble in dread, and with no means to atone, we humbly submit this plea.

Though our family lineage is one of scholars and our duty lies in taking the imperial examinations, our understanding is obscured, our wisdom and conduct imperfect. Though we strive diligently day and night, our path remains blocked, our reputation and ambitions unfulfilled, and expectations only deepen. Without supplication, how then could our aspirations ever be realized?

Yet we acknowledge that rise and fall are ordained by fate, and wealth or nobility are decreed by Heaven. To do good is to invite blessings, and only with utmost sincerity can one move the heavens. We dare to offer earnest prayer, pouring forth our pure devotion, seeking to establish merit and hope for even the slightest advancement.

Though our virtues are shallow and our faults persist, we vow to amend through repentance. We shall strictly adhere to the master’s teachings, rectify our past, and cultivate our future, thus inviting extraordinary blessings and preserving the scholar’s path.

We have heard that the **Yuánshǐ** [Primordial Sage] issued his teachings, expounding the **Twenty-Seven Grades of Ritual Offerings**, spreading among mortals to widely encourage goodness, employing skillful means to save all, and guiding even the most hardened souls—transforming their barren nature into the suitability of the Dao, and awakening their dullness into enlightened clarity.

Relying on this boundless grace, we presumptuously hope for transformation. We now humbly submit to Your Excellency, beseeching you to grant our petition and bestow your endorsement.

We, the humble subject, though lacking in talent and failing to grasp the profound truths, are unable to endure the sight of the common folk’s earnest pleas. The people’s sincerity is evident, and it is fitting to explain its meaning.

Seeing these common folk in their devout petitions, we are deeply moved by their virtue, yet find their words insufficient to convey their depth. The common folk are the masses. We now humbly present our respects, praying to the **Primordial Celestial Officials**—the **Supreme Lord Lao**, the **Supreme Elderly One**, the **Celestial Master**, the **Female Celestial Master**, the **Three Celestial Teachers**, and the **Five *Qi* Lords**—that they may kindly attend to and examine this memorial submitted by the lowly scholar. May it be granted audience by the Heavenly Court, so that **Confucian learning may flourish**, talents may be nurtured, **literature and culture may reach the frontiers**, and both civil and martial virtues may be cultivated. Thus, the bonds of humanity may be strengthened, filial piety and respect may be fulfilled, **teachings may be refined**, customs may be transformed, and we may hope to repay the grace of the **Celestial Transformations**.

In accordance with the established precedents of the **One Thousand Two Hundred Official Chapters**, we respectfully request the **Lord of the Scholar’s Office** to appoint **one hundred twenty officials**, overseeing the **Purple Canopy Palace**. Further, we petition the **Lord of the Eastern Well and Clarity** to grant a vacancy of one *hé* (合) to be filled by the lowly scholar, so that the **temperate, pure, harmonious, and virtuous *qi*** may enter and permeate the **one hundred twenty nodes** of our body, dispersing throughout the **liver and diaphragm**, renewing our resolve, cleansing the **five *zàng* organs** (心, 肝, 脾, 肺, 腎), stabilizing our spirit, guarding our **True *Qi****, dispelling the **Three Corpses** (三尸), exterminating the **Nine Parasites** (九虫), purifying falsehood and establishing truth, removing turbidity and embracing clarity, turning away from death toward life, averting misfortune and inviting blessing. Thus, the scholar may attain **open and clear-minded aspiration**, comprehend the **Sacred Principles**, excel in **literary composition**, and achieve success in studies.

Next, we request the **Lord of the *Kǒng* Vitality of the Five Classics** to appoint **one hundred twenty officials**, overseeing the **Nine Marvels Palace**, to **enlighten the scholar’s mind**, ensure retention of teachings, and cultivate **discriminative wisdom**, setting him apart from others.

Next, we request the **Celestial Kings and Jade Women**, **one thousand two hundred in number**, clad in **green robes**, to oversee the **ten thousand officials** under the scholar’s jurisdiction, bestowing upon them **seals and sashes**, enabling their movements, and granting them **divine clarity**.

We also request the **Jade Calendar and White Women**, **one thousand two hundred in number**, clad in **red robes**, to **collect and record the scholar’s soul and vital essence**, attaching them to our form, inscribing our names in the **Jade Calendar’s Mysterious Register**, and marking our **destined lifespan** on the **Crimson Book’s records**.

If the scholar seeks to **pursue official rank and fulfill his ambitions**, we pray to the **Celestial Hosts of Past Merit**, the **Deities of Noble Office and Honor**, and the **Literary Stars of the Southern Dipper’s Eastern Wall**, the **Hall of Records and Scriptures**, that they may **bestow auspicious signs**, radiate brilliance, and shower **blessings of merit and virtue**, granting us **success in examinations**.

If the scholar wishes to **present his local records** and **assist in the imperial examinations**, we pray to the **Deities of the Underworld** who govern this, and to the **local land deities**, who are **wise and just**, to **oversee the examination halls**, evaluate our **scholarly and moral conduct**, distinguish merit from mediocrity, and demonstrate **impartial fairness**. Thus, the scholar’s **learning and conduct may daily improve**, and **auspicious blessings may gather**, ensuring **advancement without hindrance**, **safety in the examination halls**, **recognition on the Golden Imperial List**, and **virtue inscribed in the Jade Hall**. May all our wishes be fulfilled, all blessings bestowed, our family **transmit purity and honor**, our loyalty to the state **be acknowledged**, our **scholarly lineage endure**, and **Confucian traditions flourish**, as a testament to the **unfailing grace of the Dao**.

**Seal of the Circular Petition**:
*"The previous memorial was amended to read: ‘The Three Realms’ Primordial Venerable One, both internally and externally."*

The **Supreme Dao of the Boundless Ultimate**, the **Highest Venerable Lord of the Golden Threshold**, humbly receives the inner seal:

*"To the Jade Sovereign of the Supreme Dao,*
*With this yellow silk and vermilion seal,*
*Humbly presented to the Highest Venerable Lord."*

The **Highest Venerable Lord**, the **Supreme Jade Sovereign**, humbly receives the outer seal:

*"To the Supreme Jade Sovereign of the Highest Purity,*
*In this wooden box—*
*Using clear yellow silk or satin,*
*Sealed with a pouch,*
*Bound by a sash as the closure,*
*Whereupon the Highest Venerable Lord shall inscribe the talisman and seal.*
*A single wooden box of yellow silk and vermilion seal,*
*Presented to the Highest Purity Celestial Axis Hall,*
*Humbly petitioning the Celestial Court,*
*To guide and introduce the Supreme Jade Sovereign of the Highest Purity."*

The Highest Venerable Lord’s seal does not bear the title *"Humbly receives the protection"*—
For though some make double or triple wooden boxes,
While they may seem refined,
When handling the vermilion seal,
They do not wish to linger long.
Layered wooden boxes,
Fire’s force cannot fully reach them,
And once the seal is applied,
It is contrary to human nature to be fully at ease.
If the wooden box is well-made,
Yet some seal it with wax,
This is even more forbidden.
For burning paper is not to be done with lamp flames—
How much more so for petitions and seals?
Wax, when near fire, melts and stains—
How can one apply the same standard as the mundane world?

**Supplication to the Nine Celestial Sovereigns of the Golden Threshold**

The Highest Venerable Lord’s seal does not bear the title *"Humbly receives the protection"*—
For though some make double or triple wooden boxes,
While they may seem refined,
When handling the vermilion seal,
They do not wish to linger long.
Layered wooden boxes,
Fire’s force cannot fully reach them,
And once the seal is applied,
It is contrary to human nature to be fully at ease.
If the wooden box is well-made,
Yet some seal it with wax,
This is even more forbidden.
For burning paper is not to be done with lamp flames—
How much more so for petitions and seals?
Wax, when near fire, melts and stains—
How can one apply the same standard as the mundane world?

---

**Supplication to the Nine Celestial Sovereigns**

The Daoist adept Lu Yuan-su of the Crude Retreat in Western Shu assembles this text.
Hu Xiang-long of the True Seclusion in Zhuling compiles and edits it.

**Petitions and seals:** Paper measuring one *chi* and two *cun* in height.
**The Nine Celestial Sovereigns’ Imperial Title:**
*Dongzhen* Great Dao, Golden Threshold, Naturally Highest Venerable,
Great Sage, Primordial Heavenly Venerable of the Golden Threshold.

**Primordial Heavenly Venerable** first transformed the Three Realms from the single *Qi* (vital breath),
And in the initial *eon* of the Dragon-Han era,
He expounded the *Dongzhen* Dao,
Enlightening both humans and celestial beings,
Thus becoming the ancestor of all Ways.

**Dongxuan** Great Dao, Jade Seat, Primordial Heavenly Venerable Dao Lord,
Great Sage, Spirit-Treasury Heavenly Venerable of the Golden Threshold.

**Dao Lord** descended to the Idyllic Heavenly Realm of Yu Fen,
And received instruction from the Primordial Heavenly Venerable.
In the *eon* of Chi Ming (Red Brilliance),
He expounded the *Dongxuan* Dao,
Enlightening and liberating all beings.

**Dongshen** Great Dao, Golden Threshold, Mysterious Primordial Sage Lord,
Great Sage, Heavenly Venerable of the Golden Threshold.

**Sage Lord** originated at the dawn of creation,
And served as the Imperial Preceptor through the ages.
In the *eon* of Kai Huang (Opening Brilliance),
He expounded the *Dongshen* Dao,
Received the teachings of the Primordial Heavenly Venerable,
And descended to Shang and Zhou epochs,
Enlightening and guiding all beings.

**Heavenly Sovereign of the Jade Emperor’s Imperial Court**
The Jade Emperor is the Heavenly Sovereign venerated at the court’s Round Mound.
He is the True Martial One who speaks of creation.
I, His attendant, have only seen in the Communing Hall of Light,
A dense and billowing red cloud—
This is when the Heavenly Sovereign descends in person.
I have never glimpsed His imperial form.

**The Purple Enclosure Celestial Sovereign of the Imperial Court**
Within the mouth of the Pleiades constellation,
There is a star called the Celestial Sovereign,
Whose spirit is named *Yao Po* (Resplendent Essence).
He truly rules over all celestial beings.

**The Northern Pole Celestial Sovereign of the Imperial Court**
The Northern Pole contains five stars,
With the central one being the Purple Enclosure Celestial Sovereign,
Also called the *Beichen* (Northern Dipper),
Thus it is said that all stars bow to him as he resides in his place.
The four surrounding stars are His ministers,
Emerging to measure degrees and receive rectification.

**The Earthly Sovereign of the Jade Emperor’s Imperial Court**
The Earthly Sovereign is the one venerated at the court’s Square Mound.
She is the *Hou Tu* (Posterior Soil),
The Earthly Sovereign honored by the king.
The king venerates Her in union with the Heavenly Sovereign,
As the Celestial Father and Earthly Mother.

---

**Supplication for the Nine Celestial Sovereigns**

With the full title of *Gaogong* (Highest Venerable),
Your humble servant petitions the Golden Threshold’s Celestial Sovereigns,
That on a certain day and hour,
At a certain place,
I may establish a Daoist assembly,
And at the *zi* hour of a certain day,
Conduct a certain *jiao* (expiatory ritual),
To invite the descent of the Highest Venerables for a full session.
Now, with the hall prepared and the ritual implements solemnly raised,
I humbly petition the Daoist scriptures,
To assist in my salvation and guidance,
And to ensure that all who take refuge
Dare not remain unprotected.

Your humble servant is sincerely fearful and trembling,
Prostrating himself with utmost reverence.

I hope to bend Your divine compassion,
To gaze upon the humble affairs of mortals,
And to extend Your boundless creation
With pity and grace,
To incline Your benevolent light
And descend Your favor,
Thus fulfilling the hopes of both humans and celestial beings,
And granting blessings to my family, my nation,
And all the hidden and manifest realms.
May my *jiao* ritual thus be harmonious and complete.

Your humble servant, with no greater aspiration than to gaze upon the heavens
And to express his most fervent and humble longing,
Dares to submit this supplication.

---

**Template for Petitions**

**Year, Month, Day**
With the full title of *Gaogong* (Highest Venerable),
Your humble servant petitions the Golden Threshold’s Celestial Sovereigns.

**Submission of Petition and Seal**

Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*,
Dares to submit this petition and seal.
The petition and seal are enclosed in the *Fanghan* (square wooden box),
And the submission follows this format.
The petition is to be delivered in person.

**Seal for the Golden Threshold’s Celestial Sovereigns**
Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*,
Dares to submit this seal to the Imperial Court.

**Supplication for the Nine Celestial Sovereigns**
Only one copy of this supplication is to be made for the *jiao* ritual,
And this format is to be used.
The seal is to be submitted as before.

**Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*.**

I humbly reflect that,
From the outset of my oath,
I have vowed to uphold and propagate the marvelous Dao,
And to rescue all beings.
All who take refuge
Shall not be left in neglect.

I now submit this petition,
That in my locality and residence,
On a certain day and hour as before,
The hall is prepared and the secret rituals commenced.
I await Your celestial mercy,
And Your gracious descent,
To grace my assembly with Your presence.

---

**Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*,**
Dares to submit this supplication in bold transgression.

**Year, Month, Day**
Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*,
Submits this supplication.

**Template for Petitions and Seals for Use in Communing with the Heavens**

**Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*.**

I humbly submit this supplication,
That in my locality and residence,
On a certain day and hour as before,
The hall is prepared and the secret rituals commenced.

I, though unworthy, am listed among the True Attendants,
And my duty is to save and guide.
I now petition on behalf of the deceased,
The departed souls of the *Yi Hang* (One Row),
And all beings of the Six Realms,
To invoke the Supreme’s符命 (*fu ming* decrees),
The golden scriptures and white tablets,
And the cloud-inscribed seals and edicts,
Thus extending salvation and rescue to them.

I fear that the departed,
If their netherworldly judgments remain unexpiated,
And they are detained in the nightly offices,
Shall have no means to disperse,
And this will hinder their liberation.

I dare to submit this supplication to the Primordial Heavenly Venerable,
With the full title of *Gaogong*,
To the Golden Threshold’s Celestial Sovereigns,
Humbly hoping for Your special compassion and consideration,
To grant my petition,
And issue an imperial decree to the Eastern Tai Mountain Bureau,
To inform the Earth and Water departments,
And all subordinate offices,
That for the deceased,
The crimes of *Wanguo* (certain deceased)
Shall be pardoned and their offenses absolved,
And they shall all be granted renewal,
To attend the Daoist assembly,
And partake in its merits and virtues.
Thus, they may further hope to spread the Dao’s *Qi*,
And receive protection from the seals and edicts,
And may all officials know to obey and follow.

Your humble servant dares to transgress against Heaven’s威 (*wei* might),
And is overwhelmed with fear and trembling.
I submit this supplication.

**Year, Month, Day**
Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*,
Submits this supplication.

**Submission to the Bureau of the Celestial Pivot**

For the *Xiaozai* (disaster-dispelling) and other Daoist assemblies (*jiào*), the phrase "female Qing" (女青) shall be omitted, reducing the original text by four characters.

Your humble servant, with the full title of *Gaogong*, does not presume to call himself "subject." Hereby, I submit this petition, aligning with the *Jiǔhuáng Biǎo* (Nine Sovereigns' Edict), to the point of completion.

Now, with solemn reverence for the altar and its sacred precincts (*tán chán*), at the first performance of the ritual procedures (*kēyí*), I shall report matters to the Nine Celestial Ones (*Jiǔqīng*). This necessarily involves the Bureau of the Celestial Pivot (*Shūniǔ Yuàn*). I humbly send this supplication for the Holy Edict (*shèng biǎo*) in several copies, praying for its transmission to the *Tianshī* (Celestial Master) to establish the teachings, so that all may follow and comply.

All official documents must be authenticated by the Celestial Office (*xiānzhí*). I submit this petition to the Bureau of the Celestial Pivot (*Shūniǔ Yuàn*), requesting the Three Heavens (*Sāntiān*) to uphold the teachings, the *Zhèngyī* (Orthodox Unity) to assist the Mysterious, and the *Jìngyīng Zhēnjūn* (Responsive True Lord) to act accordingly.

I pray for the Holy Benevolence (*shèngcí*), that this petition may be granted, and all subsequent ritual documents, once the Daoist rites are completed, shall be entrusted to the *Zhèngshén* (Direct Gods) for transmission to the Celestial Bureau (*xiānfǔ*) to be heard.

For the solemn rites (*yán*), the *Nǚqīng Zhào* (Female Qing Edict) and all provincial documents (*dūshěng wénliè*), I pray for Your mercy upon the unenlightened (*fánmèi*), to secretly invoke Your sacred authority (*wēiguāng*). All matters solemnly declared shall be known to follow and comply.

Upon the completion of the ritual assembly (*jiào xí*), I await the descent of the *Zhēnshǔ* (True Seal), hoping for Your presence to witness the oath and rituals (*zhèngméng xiūfèng*). I dare to transgress the sacred authority (*wēilíng*), overwhelmed with fear and trembling. I submit this petition.

**Official Petitions and Declarations**

**General Petitions**
If using a **Three Realms Declaration** (*Sānjiè Dìé*), follow this format.
If only submitting a **General Petition** (*Dūdié*) to the Sacred Ones, use the following format—**do not** further write on this white paper.

For the **Supreme Mysteries Bureau** (*Tàixuān Dūshěng*) conducting rituals in the **Domain of the True Officials** (*Lǐyù Zhēnguān*):
If within a **Daoist Hall** (*guàn*), invoke the **Hall-Protecting Dragon Spirit of the Dao** (*Hùdào Lóngshén*).
According to one’s native district and residence, offer sincere devotion as before, until the ritual is complete.

Now, having purified and prepared the **Celestial Altar** (*Huātán*), we proceed with the **Lawful Affairs** (*fǎshì*).
We fear that **heavenly and human intentions may diverge**, and that sincere devotion may fail to reach its mark. Given the **humble nature of mortal bonds**, there may be offenses requiring **formal reprimand** (*yíwén*).
**Petition** is hereby submitted for **detailed examination** of the matter, to be **urgently reported** to the **Celestial Vault** (*shàngqióng*).

We humbly request the **dispatch of Celestial Officials** to oversee the **fasting rites**, and further **maintain solemn silence** in the ritual grounds, **reverently awaiting** the **Sacred Procession** (*Jǐngyú*), lest there be **delay or offense against Heaven’s Will** (*tiānwēi*).
Upon completion of the fast, we shall not forget to **fulfill our pledge in faith**—thus, this petition is submitted.

Upon receipt, this petition shall be **duly executed**.

**Memorial Text (Yòu)**:
By imperial decree, I am ordered to deliver the **Rites of the Five-Peaks Dao Assembly (Luótiān Jiào Fēnkē Yí)** and request further review and annotation by this official.

I humbly submit that **fragrant incense ascends to the heavens**,
hoping to express **sincere devotion (jīngchéng)**;
when **True Saints (Zhēnshèng)** descend in grace,
they surely expect **harmonious resonance (tōnggǎn)**.

Given the **complexity of the true rites (zhēnkē)**,
and the **Daoist tradition’s reliance on precedent (yīnréng)**,
I now present this to the **enlightened and sagacious (ruìmíng)**,
trusting they will refine these **mystic secrets (mì’ào)**.

I humbly pray to the **Emperor’s Majesty**:
In matters of the Dao, you **revere antiquity (qǐgǔ)**,
and in speech, you **align with the Celestial (zètīan)**.
You honor the **hundred spirits (bǎishén)** at the **Round Mound (Yuánqiū)***,
venerate the **Seven Patriarchs (qīzǔ)** in the **Pure Temple (Qīngmiào)***,
open the **wearied halls of the Jade Purity (Yùqīng)***,
and exalt the **blessed courts of the Manifest Response (Zhāoyìng)***.

At the **Palace of the True (Huìzhēn)**, you **inspect the Jade Registers (jiǎn Yuánqiū yùjiè)***;
in the **Great Tranquility Lodge (Tàiníng)**, you **guard the Yellow Seal (shěn Fāngzé huángcóng)***.
Now that the **Five-Peaks Dao Assembly (Luótiān Jiào)** rites are being revised,
and the **Golden Seal Assembly (Jīnzhòu)** rites are being established anew,
I still fear that **ritual errors (kēyí zhuǎnwù)** or **rank discrepancies (pǐnwèi cānchā)***
may persist, so I command **羽衣 (Yǔyī)***—
to **carve and publish the sacred grades (zài bǎozhì)***.

I also order the **confused and unenlightened (míwèi)***
to **prepare further discussion (fùbèi táolùn)***.

I await the **virtuous response (shàng déyīn)***,
and **devoutly abide by Your decree (qián zūn zhào zhì)**.

This official has now **revised and compiled the Nine Volumes of the Five-Peaks Dao Assembly’s Sacred Grades (Luótiān Shèngwèi Jiǔjuàn)***,
and **assembled the Five-Peaks Dao Assembly Rites (Luótiān Kēyí)** in one volume,
**marking it at the beginning (biāo yú juànshǒu)***.

Though I am **ashamed of my limited understanding (dān fánmù)***,
I **dare to glimpse the true hierarchy (qiè zhēnjiē)***—
as a **Daoist disciple (fèngtiān tú)**, I **look upward to the Purple Purity (Zǐqīng)***,
and in **divining the Han (Cè Hàn)**, I **cannot fathom the celestial order (mò qióng yú xiān tǒng)***.
I **obey Your celestial throne (shàngzhùn shìntāo)***,
and **offer these rites in humble reverence (shāobèi cháoxiū)**.

The **Five-Peaks Dao Assembly Rites (Luótiān Kēyí)** consist of **ten volumes of grades (pǐnwèi gòng shíjuàn)***,
and I now **respectfully submit them for Your approval (jǐn shàngjìn)**.

I **humbly pray that Your Majesty** **command the Bureau of Literature (Chóngwén Yuàn)***
and its **Three Lodges (Sānguǎn)**,
**Superintendent Liu Chóngshuò (Liú Chóngshuò)***
to **transcribe fifteen copies (huànxiě shísān běn)***,
**bind and deliver them (zhuāngdì sòng)** to this official’s residence,
**sealed with the Daoist Canon’s official imprint (yòng Dàozàng yìn fèng)***—
and then **dispatch them to the Palaces of the True (Huìzhēn)**,
**Great Tranquility (Tàiníng)**,
**Jade Purity (Yùqīng)**,
**Supreme Purity (Tàiqīng)**,
and **Great Peace (Tàipíng)***,
so that **reverence may be upheld eternally (shèngfèng yǒng jiàn fúxiáng)***,
and **blessings may be perpetually offered (shèng jiàn fúxiáng)**.

I have **respectfully prepared this memorial (jǐn jù zàowén)**,
and **submit it for Your review (jǐn zào)**.

**Imperial Edict (Pīdá)**:
*"Memorial received (shěng zào jù zhī)."*

The Emperor, **solely relying upon the numinous and auspicious (Zhǐhé Língxiū)**, **reveres the wondrous scriptures (Qīnchóng Miàoběn)**.
**Granting respite to all under heaven (Zài yòu wàn guó)**, **hoping to bring them lasting prosperity (Jì dǐ yú Fùkāng)**;
**Cherishing and soothing the myriad deities (Huáiróu bǎishén)**, **thus extending blessings to them (Yòng yán yú Huīshī)**.
**It is only through the grand establishment of the True Lodges (Wéi hóngkāi yú Zhēnguǎn)**, **that strict reverence must be upheld in the ritual observances (Dāng yánfèng yú Zhāikē)**.
**May the teachings preserved in the Canon’s repositories (Yuánbāo Dàozàng zhī suǒchuán)** be **fully retained as in ancient models (Bèi cún xī fàn)**;
**So that the Daoists may consult and compare them (Bǐ yǔrén zhī cānjiào)**, **and thus harmonize their devout intentions (Shù xié jīngxīn)**.
**The Emperor’s command is hereby reiterated to the ministers (Shēn mìng fǔchén)**, **and they are charged to scrutinize them carefully (Zhòng jiā yànshì)**.

**You, esteemed scholar (Qīng)**, **mastering the halls of learning (Bó tōng xuéfú)** and **delving into the Daoist principles (Yánwèi Dàoshū)**, **having gathered these texts (Jì jiǎn yǐ sīchéng)**, **now submit them in this memorial (Huàn xiē zhāng ér lái shàng)**.
**Your diligence is truly commendable (Gōngqīn suǒ zhì)**, **and your virtues are deeply esteemed (Jiāshàng liángshēn)**.
**The memorial is known to Us (Suǒ zào zhī yú)**, **and We have pondered it for three days (Yīyī sān rì)**.

**Imperial Edict (Yùzhì Kējì Shī cì Zǐsūn Xūbái lùn zào xiàn qiánmǎ shì)**:
*"For those who observe fasts and rituals (Fàn xiūzhāo), and present money and horses (zào xiàn qiánmǎ),*
**it is sufficient to demonstrate sincerity and loyalty (Zhǐ yǐ zhìchéng xiàoxìn, Tōngdá Zhēnlíng)**.
**If the ranks are divided too widely (Ruò fēnwèi shāo duō)**, **then all matters will fall short (Jí zhūshì yǒu quē)**.
**Ancient methods merely burned incense and cut hair (Gǔfǎ dàn fénchái gēfà)**, **presented offerings with flying memorials (Zào bì fēizhāng)**, **offered libations and flowers (Zhuóshuǐ xiànhuā)**, **and prayed with focused hearts (Míngxīn kǎn dǎo)**.
**From this, it is evident (Yóu cǐ guānzhī)** that **the method of presenting memorials (Zào zhǐ zhī fǎ)** **also does not require excessive offerings to attain blessings (Yì bù jiǎ duō ér huò fú)**—**it lies solely in utmost sincerity (Zhǐ zài zhìchéng yǐ yǐ)**.

**According to the *Daozàng* (Àn Dàozàng)**,*
**the Three Lodges’ rituals (Sānguǎn zhāikē)** are as follows:
- **The Upper Element Gold Lodges Fast (Shàngyuán Jīn guàn zhāo)**, **observed by the sovereign (Dìzhǔ xiūfèng)**, **with elaborate rites to match the heavens (Zhǎnlǐ pèitiān)**, **and the grand dispensation of the Great Universal Ritual (Bàisàn shè Pǔtiān Dàzhāo)** with **three thousand six hundred divisions (Sānqiān liùshí fēnwèi)**;
- **The Middle Element Jade Lodges Fast (Zhōngyuán Yù guàn zhāo)**, **for the protection and blessing of the Six Palaces (Bǎoyòu Liùgōng)**, **and the support of the Consorts and Empress (Fǔníng Fèihòu)**, **with the grand dispensation of the Great Heavenly Cycle Ritual (Bàisàn shè Zhōutiān Dàzhāo)** with **two thousand four hundred divisions (Èrqiān sìbǎi fēnwèi)**;
- **The Lower Element Yellow Lodges Fast (Xiàyuán Huángdié zhāo)**, **for common folk to observe (Chénshù tōngxiū)**, **universally benefiting the family and state (Pǔzī jiāguó)**, **with the grand dispensation of the Great Celestial Ritual (Bàisàn shè Luótiān Dàzhāo)** with **one thousand two hundred divisions (Yīqiān èrbǎi fēnwèi)**.

**The ascending and descending order (Yòu Sānguǎn zhāo shēngjiàng cìdì)**, **along with the sacred titles and ranks (Jí shèngzhēn wèihào)**, **were established in the *Dàzhōng Xiángfú* era (Nǎi Dàzhōng Xiángfú nián)**, **by imperial decree (Zhuàn tuī Zhōngxié Cóngtóng Dézuǒ Lígōngchén Xiàng Wáng Qīnrú zhòngxiū dìng)**, **and promulgated to the palaces in the capital (Bānxià zài jīng gōngguàn)**, **as well as to the renowned mountains and blessed lands across the empire (Bìng tiānxià míngshān fúdì shōudiǎn)**, **to serve the court’s observances (Yǐ bèi cháoting xiūfèng)**.
**Should great ministers perform rituals for the state (Huò dàchén wéi guó)**, **they may also set them up (Yǐxǔ xiūshè)**;
**Commoners are not permitted to observe them (Shùrén bùxǔ fèngxiū)**.

**Additionally, the recent imperial decrees (Yòu jìnxiàng Huángdì běnmìng)**, **including the *Tiānníng Jié* (Tiānníng Jié)**, **mandate seven annual rituals (Zhúnián qī cì)**.
**The regional governors and military prefects (Fānfāng Jiézhèn)** are to **establish the Gold Lodges Dao-field (Xiūjiàn Jīn guàn Dàochǎng)** and **dispense the ritual with three hundred sixty divisions (Bàisàn shè Zhāo Sānbǎi liùshí fēnwèi zhǐ)**.

**The sacred ranks and their prescribed rituals (Shèngwèi jù zài xīnxiàng kējì)** are **permanently fixed (Yǒng wéi dìngshì)**.
**The *Língbǎo* Dao-field (Língbǎo Dàochǎng)**, **which pertains to the rites of disaster elimination, spirit elevation, and chapter offerings (Jì xiāozāi qiān bái bǎizhāng)**, **is limited to one hundred twenty divisions (Yībǎi èrshí fēnwèi zhǐ)**.
**The *Língbǎo* Heavenly Sovereign Fast (Língbǎo Tiāngōng zhāo)**, **as well as the forty-eight altars of the minor ritual (Sìshíbāi tán xiǎozhāo)**, **for presenting money and horses (Zào xiàn qiánmǎ)**:
- **Twenty-four divisions (Èrshísì fēn)**, **thirty-six divisions (Sānshíliù fēn)**, **forty-two divisions (Sìshí'èr fēn)**, **sixty divisions (Liùshí fēn)**, **seventy-two divisions (Qīshí'èr fēn)**, **and one hundred twenty divisions (Yībǎi èrshí fēn)**.

**These prescribed rites (Yòu jiàn yìshì)** are **all in accordance with the ritual canons (Bìng yuē kējì)** and **the newly promulgated court models (Jí cháoting xīnbān yìfàn)**.
**They are to be arranged in concise and orderly sequence (Bìng lìng shìjié wén)**, **to facilitate observance (Yǐ biàn xiūfèng)**—**they must not exceed these numbers (Bùkě guò cǐ shù yě)**.

**Furthermore, the *Ānzhèng Tiānshī* method of preserving the Sovereign’s original command (Běnmìng cúnxiūfǎ yún)** states:
*"For every division of memorial paper (Zào zhǐ yī fēn)**, **one must use fine paper to depict a horse (Dāng yòng hào zhǐ huà mǎ yī pǐ)**, **and one attendant (Zhuī yī rén ér yǐ)**, **to represent one person (Dàixíng yī rén bù huà kǒu)**.
**From this, it is clear (Yóu cǐ guānzhī)** that **the money and horses now presented (Jīn suǒ zào xiàn qiánmǎ)** **do not conform to the ritual standards (Yì wèi hé yìgé)**—**they are merely wasteful expenditures (Tú yǒu fèiyòng)** that **serve only to invite censure (Shì yǐ zhāoqiàn ér yǐ)**.
**Moreover, common folk often present memorials with adorned images of dragons, cranes, stars, and earthly deities (Shìrén duō zào zhuānghuà lónghè xīngxiàng, Tiāndì shénqí)**—**this is the most erroneous of all (Cǐ yóu mímiù zhī shèn)**.
**Exhaustively examining the scriptures and ritual canons (Piànjiǎn jīngkē)**, **there is no such format (Wèi yǒu cǐ shì)**.
**The Great Dao’s boundless expanse (Dàluó liángkuò)**, **and the revered sacred (Shàngshèng zūnchóng)**, **are such that a single devout thought (Yīniàn cáixīng)** arises, **and the spirits respond in kind (Suí jī qù gǎn)**—**how could excessive money and horses bring blessings (Qǐ duō zào qiánmǎ ér huò fúyòu yě)**?
**Ancient practices established their methods (Gǔrén shèfǎ)** **solely to manifest sincerity and loyalty (Wéi yǐ biǎoshì xiàoxīn)**, **to repent and atone for sins (Chànqiān shúguò)**, **and to inspire true devotion (Shǐ rén yǒu xìng xiàng zhī chéng)**.
**Yet, it is also indispensable to present offerings (Yòu bùkě bù zào xiàn yě)**.
**Only the enlightened and wise (Wéi míngzhé zhī shì)** should **examine and follow them diligently (Xiáng ér xíngzhī)**.

**Attendant (Zhuī)**, **from the character *念 (niàn)***, **refers to those who serve in attendance (Shìfòng yě)**.

**The Nine Sovereigns’ Memorial Format (Jiǔhuáng Jìnzhàngshì)**:
**A Daoist of prescribed rank (Fèngdào jùwèi chén)** submits **his surname (xìng)**, **money (qián)**, **horses (mǎ)**, and **dragon chariots (lóngchē)**.
**This official (Yòu chén)** **respectfully and carefully presents them (Qǐn jǐn shàngjìn yǐ wén)**.

**Memorial Format (Yòu chén jǐn jǐn shàngjìn yǐ wén)**:
**Sealed Circular Envelope (Yuánfēngshì)**:
*"A memorial from the Daoist of prescribed rank (Shènghào Jīnguān xià Fèngdào jùwèi chén xìng)* **respectfully presented (Zào xiàn jǐn jǐn shàngfēng)**,
**with the surname of the official omitted (Fānghánshì bùshǐ chén zì)**.
**One memorial case (Jìnzhàng yī hán)** **is respectfully presented (Qǐn jǐn shàng yì)**.
**To the High Master of Half-Court Rank (Gāogōng bàn yù xìng)** **respectfully sealed (Qǐn fēng)**,
**for introduction to the Upper Clarity Heavenly Axis Academy (Shàngqīng Tiāngōngyuàn yǐnjìn)**,
**and the submission of memorials by the assembled spirits (Zhòngzhēn xiànzhàngshì)**."

**Memorial of the Daoist of Prescribed Rank (Fèngdào jùwèi xìng)**

*"The Daoist of prescribed rank, surname [omitted], with [designated] number of coins and horses. Hereby respectfully petitions the Sacred Title (Shènghào), humbly awaiting the True Benevolence (Zhēncí) to condescend and graciously accept this memorial. Respectfully submitted.*

**Memorial of the Daoist of Prescribed Rank, surname [omitted]**
*[Year] [Month] [Day]*

**Sealed Circular Envelope (Yuánfēngshì) – Uniform Format for the Assembled Spirits (Zhòngzhēn tóngshì), with only the term "memorial" inscribed (zhǐ yún zhàng qǐn fēng).*

**Sacred Title**
*Memorial of the Daoist of Prescribed Rank, surname [omitted], respectfully submitted (Zào qǐn fēng).*

**Ritual Invocation of the Luo Heavenly Hosts (Luòtiān děng jiào Shènghào)**

**Yellow Talisman Ritual for Luo Heaven (Huángfù Luòtiān yībāi èrshí fēn Shèngwèi)**
- **First Memorial (5 divisions):** Spirits of the Jade Emptiness Supreme Sovereign (Yùxū Shàngdì)
  - Jade Emptiness Supreme Sovereign, issuing *The Secret Talismans of the Jade Purity (Yùqīng Mìfù)*
  - The Most High Jade Emperor, issuing *The Three Caverns’ Pearl of True Reality (Sāndòng Zhūzhēn)*
  - The Taiwei Jade Emperor, issuing *The Eight Scenes of the Golden Obelisk Court Assembly (Jīnquè Bājǐng Cháo Huì Tú)*
  - The Taiwei Heavenly Emperor, issuing *The Most High Secret Essentials (Wúshàng Mìyào)*
  - The Shaowei Grand Sovereign, issuing *The Most High Secret Essentials (Wúshàng Mìyào)*
  *(All henceforth referred to as True Benevolence; same thereafter.)*

- **Second Memorial (3 divisions):** Spirits under the Three Treasures Imperial Lords (Sānbǎo Dìjūn ménxià)
  - Qingwei Heavenly Treasure Lord (Qīngwēi Tiānbǎojūn)
  - Yǔyú Lingbao Lord (Yǔyú Língbǎojūn)
  - Taichì Divine Treasure Lord (Tàichì Shénbǎojūn)
  *(Issuing The Three Caverns’ Divine Talismans (Sāndòng Shénfù))*

- **Third Memorial (9 divisions):** Spirits under the Nine Heavenly Sovereigns (Jiǔtiān Shàngdì ménxià)
  - Yùdān Wúliàng Tiāndì (郁单无量天帝)
  - Shàngshàng Chánshàn Wúliàngshòu Tiāndì (上上禅善无量寿天帝)
  - Fánjiān Xūyán Tiāndì (梵监须延天帝)
  - Jìrán Dōushù Tiāndì (寂然兜术天帝)
  - Bōluóní Mìbùjiāo Lè Tiāndì (波罗尼密不骄乐天帝)
  - Dòngyuán Huàyīngshēng Tiāndì (洞元化应声天帝)
  - Línghuà Fánfǔ Tiāndì (灵化梵辅天帝)
  - Gāoxū Qīngmíng Tiāndì (高虚清明天帝)
  - Wúxiǎng Wújié Wú’ài Tiāndì (无想无结无爱天帝)
  *(Issuing The Great Possession Golden Scriptures of the Jade Purity Secret Talismans (Yùqīng Mìfù Dàyǒu Jīnshū))*

- **Fourth Memorial (5 divisions):** Spirits of the Supreme Sovereign of the Great Sun, Vermilion Clarity (Tàiyáng Zhūmíng Shàngdì)
  - Supreme Sovereign of the Great Sun, Flaming Extremity, Vermilion Clarity (Tàiyáng Yànjí Zhūmíng Shàngdì)
  - Imperial Lord of the Upper Clarity Golden Obelisk (Huángtiān Shàngqīng Jīnquè Dìjūn)
  - Highest Sovereign of the Primordial Void, Dark Origin, Supreme Emptiness (Hùndùn Tàiwú Xuánshēng Gāoshàng Xū Huángdìjūn)
  - Sovereign Lord of Azure Soul, Great Radiance, Soaring Support (Cānglíng Tàiguāng Fúyáo Dìjūn)
  - Jade Purity Golden Obelisk, Celestial Conduct, Posterior Sage Emperor (Qíngzhēn Jīnquè Fánxíng Hòushèng Dìjūn)
  *(Issuing The Eight Scenes of the Golden Obelisk Court Assembly (Jīnquè Bājǐng Cháo Huì Tú))*

- **Fifth Memorial (8 divisions):** Spirits under the Eight Sovereigns of the Eastern Quarter (Dōngfāng Bā Tiāndì ménxià)
  - Supreme Sovereign of the Great Ancestor, Yellow Ancestral Lineage (Tàihuáng Huángzēng Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Great Clarity, Jade Completion (Tàimíng Yùwán Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Pure Clarity, He Tong (Qīngmíng Hé Tóng Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Mysterious Embryo, Level Nurturing (Xuāntāi Píngyù Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Original Clarity, Literary Uprightness (Yuánmíng Wénjǔ Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Upper Clarity, Seven Luminaries, Mo Yi (Shàngmíng Qīyào Móyí Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Voidness, Exceeding the Pole (Xūwú Yuèhéng Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of the Supreme Polarity, Enshrouding Darkness (Tàijí Méngyì Tiāndì)

- **Sixth Memorial (8 divisions):** Spirits under the Eight Sovereigns of the Southern Quarter (Nánfāng Bā Tiāndì ménxià)
  - Sovereign of Crimson Clarity, Harmonious Yang (Chīmíng Héyáng Tiāndì)
  - Sovereign of Original Clarity, Reverent Splendor (Yuánmíng Gōnghuá Tiāndì)

「Yàomíng Zōngpiāo Tiāndì
　　Zhúluò Huángjiào Tiāndì
　　Xūmíng Tángyào Tiāndì
　　Guānmíng Duānjìng Tiāndì

　　Tàihuàn Jíyáo Tiāndì

- **Seventh Memorial (8 divisions):** Spirits under the Eight Sovereigns of the Western Quarter (Xīfāng Bā Tiāndì ménxià)
  - Yàomíng Zōngpiāo Tiāndì
  - Zhúluò Huángjiào Tiāndì
  - Xūmíng Tángyào Tiāndì
  - Guānmíng Duānjìng Tiāndì
  - Xuānmíng Gōngqìng Tiāndì
  - Tàihuàn Jíyáo Tiāndì

- **Eighth Memorial (8 divisions):** Spirits under the Eight Sovereigns of the Northern Quarter (Běifāng Bā Tiāndì ménxià)
  - Hào Tíng Xiàodù Tiāndì
  - Yuāntōng Yuāndòng Tiāndì
  - Tàiwén Hànchǒng Miàochéng Tiāndì
  - Tàisù Xiùlè Jīnshàng Tiāndì
  - Tàixū Wúshàng Chángróng Tiāndì
  - Tàishì Yùlóng Téngshèng Tiāndì
  - Lóngbiàn Fàndù Tiāndì
  - Tàijí Píngyù Jiǎyì Tiāndì (rightly emerging from *The Sutra of Infinite Salvation*)

- **Ninth Memorial (16 divisions):** Spirits of the Primordial Holy Mother Yuanjun and the Nine Truths (Xiāntiān Shèngmǔ Yuánjūn Zhòngzhēn)
  - Primordial Holy Mother Yuanjun of the Nine Truths and the Supreme One (Xiāntiān Tàihòu Tàiyī Yuánjūn)
    As seen in the Green Sheep Palace stele and *The True Record*, and further in the *Tàiqīng Yún* ("Supreme Clarity Clouds"), the Primordial Holy Mother Yuanjun governs the ranks of immortals. Thus, she is first in title. Originally, the Mysterious and Marvelous Jade Maiden (Xuānmìo Yùnǚ) of the Mixed Primordial Sovereign (Hùnyuán Dìjūn) was entrusted with gestation and descent, ascending to become the Primordial Holy Mother Yuanjun.
    The Tang Emperor Xuānzōng (Táng Mínghuáng) posthumously honored her as the Primordial Holy Mother, though she was originally titled Primordial Holy Mother Yuanjun. She is commonly referred to as the Primordial Yuanjun Empress (Xiāntiān Yuánhòu), though the source of this designation remains unclear; hence, both are recorded.

    - Nine Spirits, Supreme Marvelous White Jade Tortoise Platform, Night Radiance Golden Truth, Ten Thousand *Qi* Holy Mother Yuanjun (Jiǔlíng Tàimiào Báiyù Guìtái Yèguāng Jīnzhēn Wànqì Shèngmǔ Yuánjūn)
    - Supreme Female One, Imperial Truth of the Nine Lights (Wúshàng Cīyī Dìzhēn Jiǔguāng Shèngmǔ)
    - Highest Voidness, Mysterious Primordial Holy Mother of the Mixed Transformation (Gāoshàng Xūwú Xuānyuán Hùnhuà Chūzhēn Shèngmǔ)
    - Three Heavenly Yang Spirits, Supreme Mother of the Supreme Polarity (Sāntiān Yánghún Tàijí Shèngmǔ)
    - Vermilion Radiance, Dark Yin Dual Scenery Holy Mother (Zhūguāng Dòngyīn Èrjǐng Shèngmǔ)
    - Three Substances, Dark Yin Supreme Micro Holy Mother (Sān Sù Dòngyīn Tàiwēi Shèngmǔ)
    - Great Possession, Voidness of the Mixed Chaos, Substance of the Primordial Soul, Marvelous Birth Holy Mother (Dàyǒu Kòngdòng Hùndùn Huà Sùlíng Miàoshēng Shèngmǔ)
    - Nine Flowers, Voidness of the Primordial Yang, Flying Birth Holy Mother (Jiǔhuā Kòngdòng Yuányáng Fēishēng Shèngmǔ)
    - Supreme Yin, Divine Radiance of the Mysterious Primordial, Azure Sovereign Holy Mother (Tàiyīn Shènguāng Xuānjí Qīngdì Shèngmǔ)
    - Supreme Primordial Truth, Celestial Emperor Holy Mother of the Void (Wúshàng Jízhēn Tàixū Tiānhuáng Shèngmǔ)
    - Primordial Yang, Nine Primordials, Luminous Soul, White Truth Holy Mother (Yuányáng Jiǔyuán Yùlíng Hào Zhēn Shèngmǔ)
    - North Pole, Interchange of Spirits, Azure Radiance, Supreme Emperor Holy Mother (Běijí Jiāolíng Yàoguāng Tàihuáng Shèngmǔ)
    - Voidness, Primordial Emperor, Nine Heavens, Absolute Void Holy Mother (Xūwú Yuánhuáng Jiǔtiān Juéshìng Shèngmǔ)
    - Ten Thousand *Qi*, Absolute Darkness, Purple Radiance, Recorded Holy Mother (Wànqì Juémíng Zǐguāng Lièjì Shèngmǔ)

    (Rightly emerging from *The Golden Obelisk of Eight Sceneries: Imperial Assembly Diagram*)

- **Tenth Memorial (5 divisions):** Spirits of the Primordial Three Mysteries Yuanjun and the Nine Truths (Tàiyī Sānmì Yuánjūn Zhòngzhēn)
  - Nine Heavens, Infinite Primordial Three Mysteries Yuanjun (Jiǔtiān Wúliàng Tàiyī Sānmì Yuánjūn)
  - Nine Flowers, Nine Peaceful Consorts (Jiǔhuā Ānfēi Liàngfēi) (both titles emerging from *The Great Luo Nine Heavens Diagram*)

  - Nine *Qi*, Substance-Born Consort (Jiǔqì Sùshēng Yuànfēi)
  - Eastern Hua, Spirit Consort (Dōnghuá Língfēi)
  - Great Cavern, Return to Primordial Feathered Truth (Dàdòng Huíyuán Yǔzhēn) (rightly emerging from *The Golden Obelisk of Eight Sceneries: Imperial Assembly Diagram*)

- **Eleventh Memorial (4 divisions):** Spirits under the Five Sovereigns of the Upper Clarity (Shàngqīng Qīngtóng Jūn Zhòngzhēn)
  - Upper Minister, Eastern City, Supreme Ruler of the Nine Truths (Fāngzhū Shàngxiàng Jiǔzhēn Wángjūn)
  - Supreme Administrator, Western City, Supreme Ruler (Shàngzǎi Xīchéng Zǒngzhēn Wángjūn)
  - Supreme Protector, Great Dan Palace, South Pole Yuanjun (Shàngbǎo Tàidān Gōng Nánjí Yuánjūn)
  - Supreme Attendant, White Mountain Palace, Supreme Substance Yuanjun (Shàngfù Báishān Gōng Tàisù Yuánjūn) (rightly emerging from *The Taiping Scripture*)

- **Twelfth Memorial (4 divisions):** Spirits under the Four Sovereigns of the Four Poles (Sìjí Zhēnwáng ménxià)
  - Bundled Pole Sovereign, Great Sunrise Sovereign (Shùjí Zhēnwáng Fúsāng Dàdì)
  - South Pole Sovereign, Great Dan Terrace Sovereign (Nánjí Zhēnwáng Dāníng Dàdì)
  - Western Pole Sovereign, Substance-Spirit Sovereign (Xījí Zhēnwáng Sùlíng Dàdì)
  - North Pole Sovereign, Dark Yin Cavern Sovereign (Běijí Zhēnwáng Dòngyīn Dàdì)

    (The Eastern and Southern Poles, namely Eastern Glow Sunrise and Southern Dan Terrace Sovereigns, were originally two positions in the old texts, but now are unified. This is especially so within the Four Poles Sovereigns, where the titles are repeated.)

- **Thirteenth Memorial (5 divisions):** Spirits of the Heavenly Person of the Nine Truths (Tiānzhēn Huángrén Zhòngzhēn)

**Natural Great Immortal, Heavenly Person of the Nine Truths**
Nine Elder Immortals of the Celestial Metropolis, Nine *Qi* Venerables
Heavenly Sovereign, Heavenly Venerable

*(From the *Golden Threshold: Eight Scenes of Court Assembly*)*

**The Great Vigilant Sacrificial Star Lord** sits upon the Jade Emperor’s throne. In the old texts, this was placed under the Five Elders’ Imperial Lords, namely the Imperial Lords of the Purple Enclosure (紫微), Azure Enclosure (太微), Celestial Market (天市), Celestial Horn (天角), and Great Fire (大火). It is unclear whether these are the Imperial thrones within the star-walls, for the Imperial throne of the Purple Enclosure is indeed the Heavenly Sovereign, the Great Emperor of the Northern Pole, ranked among the Nine Sovereigns, whose precedence in ceremonial order is clear.

- **Yuè Zhíshǐ** (月直使者) – Monthly Direct Attendants

*The above follow the old rituals.*

**Rightly, the *Luótiān* [1] One Thousand Two Hundred Manifestations of Sacred and True Positions**—whether compiled from the imperial court’s original edition of Three Thousand Six Hundred Manifestations or gathered from local transmissions—each version has its own merits and shortcomings.

In the midst, there are also **twofold, threefold, and even several tenfold divisions**, which are then combined into a single fold. Additionally, there are instances of **repetition in sequence** due to slight variations in sacred titles that were not carefully examined.

For example:
- **Mùgōng Shàngxiàng** [2] (东华木公上相) of the Eastern Treasure [3] is the same as **Qīngtóng Jūn Shàngxiàng** (上相青童君) of the Square Array Palaces [4];
- **Dānlíng Dàdì** (东霞扶桑丹陵大帝) of the Eastern Dawn and Pillar-Sun [5] is the same as **Zhēnwáng** (东极南极真王) of the Eastern and Southern Extremes;
- The **Five Spirits and Five Elders** (五灵五老) correspond to the **Five Directions and Five Emperors** (五方五帝) and similar cases—too numerous to enumerate.

Thus, I have taken the **originally bestowed edition** and gathered all transmitted versions, cross-referencing them in sequence, deleting redundancies, and finally arranging them according to **star stations and degrees**—though even these cannot be fully clarified. Once, I requested guidance from **Master Lǐ Zhōngdà** (二江宗丞李中大), who graciously **assigned their star stations and degrees**, demonstrating their proper sequence before me. This allowed the completion of the full collection.

Among these, the **hierarchy of sacred positions** and their **ranked orders** descend according to their original and ancient rites, carefully examined and arranged in sequence.

The so-called **repetition in sequence** arises from the **sacred position names themselves**, and each is annotated under its respective title.

**Cave and Dragon Offerings: Manifestations 24+**
- **Upper Element Bestowing Blessing Heavenly Officials** (上元赐福天官)
- **Playen Master of the Mysterious Middle** (玄中大法师)
- **Supervising Master of the Fasting** (监斋大法师)

---
**Annotations (for reference only, not part of translation):**
[1] *Luótiān* (罗天) – "Arrayed Heaven," a term for celestial hierarchies in Daoist cosmology.
[2] *Mùgōng* (木公) – "Wooden Lord," a Daoist deity associated with the Eastern Treasure.
[3] *Dōnghuà* (东华) – "Eastern Treasure," one of the Three Pure Ones' palaces.
[4] *Fāngzhū Gōng* (方诸宫) – "Square Array Palaces," a Daoist celestial bureaucracy.
[5] *Dōngxiá Fúshāng* (东霞扶桑) – "Eastern Dawn and Pillar-Sun," a sacred mountain and tree in Daoist lore.

**Dao/Way Gate Regulations, Volume Four**

**Cloud Talismans and Sacred Edicts**
**Three Sovereigns’ Inner Secrets and Hidden Scriptures**
The **Heavenly Sovereign’s** 125th and 126th characters combined, as well as the 161st and 162nd characters combined.
The **Earthly Sovereign’s** 117th and 118th characters combined.
The above formats are all derived from the **Central Alliance’s** *Jue* and *Lue* after careful collation and arrangement.

**Sacred Text to Subdue the Heavens** (extracted from the *Experience of the Huatang Inner Prohibition: Teaching to Guide Humans*)
**Eastern Azure Sovereign’s Sacred Text to Subdue the Heavens**
*In the Horn constellation, the Dragon bears the River,*
*Protecting the world and repelling evil.*
*The True King descends,*
*And all malevolence is crushed.*
*The Earthly Domain endures forever,*
*Through countless *kalpas* without decay.*

**Right Cloud Talisman:**
*I humbly petition the Azure Spirit Sovereign, the Primordial Lord of the Nine *Qi* Heavens,*
*That Your auspicious presence may arise like the dawn,*
*Your radiance envelop all lands,*
*Bringing spring to all beings,*
*Your merit equal to all creatures,*
*Gathering these myriad wonders,*
*And clustering blessings upon one.*

*Guard the Precious *Li* with boundless compassion,*
*Embody the *Kunyuan* without ceasing.*
*Humbly presented.*

*Year | Month | Day | High Official Title | Declared and Circulated*

**Southern Vermilion Sovereign’s Sacred Text to Subdue the Heavens**
*The Vermilion Sovereign commands the Spirits,*
*And all *dharma* is opened to the world.*
*Demons and ghosts are exterminated,*
*And calamities vanish from the world.*
*The Divine Talisman and Sacred Scriptures*
*Ensure the Dao/Way’s eternal prosperity.*

**Right Cloud Talisman:**
*I humbly petition the Crimson Spirit Sovereign, the True Old Lord of the Three *Qi* Heavens,*
*That the Sage’s enlightenment may shine forth,*
*And all kingdoms take him as their model.*
*The Fire King’s great *virtue/power*,*
*Like the sun and moon, equally radiant,*
*Blesses longevity from the Southern Mountains,*
*And the Heavens and Earth align in granting eternal duration.*

*Humbly presented.*

*Year | Month | Day | High Official Title | Declared and Circulated*

*The ruler’s reign serene and peaceful.*

*Channel the Dao’s flowing qi,*
*Preserve and fortify the Yellow Court.*

*Humbly presented.*

*To relocate and elevate the departed souls—*
