**Lantern Offerings for Litigation (冢讼灯牌)**
Seven lanterns are offered for each of the following:
- The seven lamps of the **Relay Inn Officials** (驿亭令, 驿亭丞, 建节监功大将军, 素车白马大将军),
- The three lamps of the **Three Palaces** (中安三宫三灯),
totaling **eighty-seven lanterns** (计八十七盏).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Ten Thousand Celestial Beings of the Three Realms and the Eight Directions** (三界万天、十方八极), beseeching the resolution of litigious disputes and severing ties of reincarnation (断除复连).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Six Heavenly Bureaus** (天曹六司) and their **Record-Keeping Officials** (掌籍官属), invoking merit registration and the erasure of deathly records (纪功录善，削死注生).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Three Officials and Five Emperors** (三官五帝) and their **Four Heavenly Bureaus** (四司曹属), harmonizing and releasing grievances, and extinguishing disputes (和释冤仇，消平注讼).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Emperor of Chengdu** (酆都大帝) and all his **officials**, petitioning for the forgiveness of ancestral sins and the release of all wrongfully imprisoned souls (原赦祖弥，一切冤囚).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Emperor of the Watery Realm** (水府大帝) and all his **officials**, dissolving calamities and oaths, and vowing to sever false alliances (消解殃考，誓绝盟言).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Five Sacred Mountains and Ten Mountains** (五岳十山) and their **Assistants of the Mandate** (佐命官属), dispelling litigation and detainment, and halting entanglements (消除讼逮，止息牵连).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the City Deities** (城隍主者) and **Divine Officials of Rituals** (祀典神祇), releasing souls from underworld prisons and lifting curses (放释幽牢，解除咒诅).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Eternal Night of the Nine Yin** (九阴长夜) and **all imprisoned souls** (诸狱幽徒), invoking their return to the Dao and ascension to pure realms (念道归真，转升净境).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **the Ancestors of Past Generations** (上代家亲) and **departed loved ones** (先亡眷属), enlightening their hearts and enabling their transcendence to human and heavenly realms (开明心地，超达人天).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **creditors and wrongdoers from past lives and the present** (前生今世、债主冤家), permanently severing grudges and granting universal liberation (永断冤雠，并皆解脱).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **external Daoist practitioners causing illness** (外道行病) and **the King of Ghosts and all malevolent spirits** (鬼王等众), urging them to abandon false thoughts and cease their oppression (各回正念，无复凭凌).

**Seven lanterns** are dedicated to **all imperfect beings suffering in the lower realms** (一切不具足、受苦众生), prompting repentance for past transgressions and enabling them to attain fullness (忏悔前非，生具足相).

**End of Volume Nine of Daoist Institutions (道门定制卷之九竟)**
**End of Volume Ten of Daoist Institutions (道门定制卷之十)**

**Volume Nine of Daoist Institutions (道门定制卷之九) continues:**

「Dedicated by the Daoist of Western Shu, Master Lü Yuansu of Puxuan, and compiled by Master Hu Xianglong of Xingyuan, the **Five Precepts Tablet for Renewing Records and Substituting Ledgers** at the Daoist Ritual Platform (太上更籍换案续命延年道场五戒坛牒).
Upon completion of the ritual, when the platform is established and observed with reverence, may all sincere and earnest practitioners—seeing this—**abandon their past misdeeds, renew their resolve, and return to the Great Dao**, seeking enlightenment and further cultivation. In accordance with the sacred rites, I now transmit the **Five Precepts of the Most High**, urging diligent observance without negligence, to bring blessings and avert calamities.

The Most High has spoken: There exist celestial officials—**the Gods of Judgment and Benevolence** (司过、司善之神)—who record human deeds of virtue and vice, thereby extending or shortening one’s lifespan. Additionally, the **Three Northern Celestial Luminaries** (三台北斗君) manifest their presence, their scattered light ever dwelling upon human heads, to chronicle each person’s merits and faults.

Furthermore, the **Three Corpses Gods** (三尸神) reside within the human body. On every **Gengshen day** (庚申日), they ascend to the **Celestial Hall of Records** (天曹) and report the person’s transgressions and sins. On the **dark moon’s day** (月晦), even the **Kitchen God** (灶君) does the same. On these days, the **Three Officials and Five Emperors** (三官五帝), **the Grand Unity of Destiny** (太一司命), the **North Dipper Officials of Ghostly Investigation** (北斗司察鬼), and the **Eight Divine Messengers of the Grand Unity** (太一八神使者) descend to the **Green Spirit Grotto and the Three Northern Yin Courts** (青灵洞阴北酆三宫), to examine the world’s living and dead—**their karmic retributions, merits, and faults**. The *Sutra of Causes and Conditions* (因缘经) states:

*The Celestial Sovereign often summons the **Child of Fate and Record** (注算童子), bearing the **Black and Green Ledgers** (青黑二簿), who traverse the mortal realm, measuring sins and virtues, and reporting them to the **Celestial Hall of Records**. The **God of Destiny** (司命) then, according to the severity of the crimes, either **shortens one’s lifespan by years** (夺纪) or **by days** (夺算). If the guilt is excessive, the suffering extends to one’s descendants. The recording of virtue and vice never ceases for an instant. For those of virtue, the **Gods of Destiny and Record** (司命、司录) grant longevity; for those of vice, the **Six Heavenly Demons** (六天魔鬼) seize their souls and spirits.*

It is also said: The lifespan of all mortals is governed by the **Earthly Officials** (地司). The **Celestial Sovereigns and Empires** (诸天诸帝), in accordance with the ledgers, determine life and death without deviation, not even by a single thread.

If one can **recognize the frailty of their virtuous power and the multitude of their sins**, fearing that the **officials of the Three Realms** (三界官属) or the **Child of Ghostly Investigation** (察命童子) may **seize their spirit-souls** (神魂), **cutting short their vital breath** (生炁), then—whether afflicted by **prolonged illness** (疾病缠绵), **severe calamities** (灾厄重困), **adverse fate** (运临凶恶), or **precarious life** (命在颠危)—they must **urgently seek purification and expiation** (修禳), **pledge wealth as proof** (割财为信), **reveal their sincere devotion** (披露丹诚), **establish a Daoist Ritual Platform** (建置道场), and **petition the Yin Courts** (咨白阴司) for **renewal of records and substitution of ledgers** (更籍换案). First, they must **acknowledge and repent their sins committed in this mortal life** (首谢所犯生身罪咎), **take the Five Precepts of the Most High** (受太上五戒), and **cultivate their spirit-souls**, thereby ensuring **longevity, tranquility, and well-being** (寿考康宁). Their **merits and virtues will be vast and unthinkable** (功德巍巍，不可思议).

Now, before the Dao, I transmit the Five Precepts:

**The First Precept** is to **cease miserly thoughts** (止息悭心) and **constantly cultivate the Daoist sanctuaries and observances** (常修宫观), **widely establish fields of merit** (广建福田), **relieve poverty and extract suffering** (济贫拔苦), **create images and copy scriptures** (造像写经), so that **longevity, tranquility, and well-being** (寿考康宁) may be secured, and **future generations flourish abundantly** (后昆繁盛).

**The Second Precept** is to **cease greedy thoughts** (止息贪心) and **constantly harbor benevolence and frugality** (常怀慈俭), **cultivate vegetarian offerings and perform expiatory rites** (修斋设醮), **practice the Dao and recite scriptures** (行道诵经), and **burn incense in praise** (烧香赞叹), so that **fields of merit become boundless** (福田无量) and **benefit all beings** (利益众生).

**The Third Precept** is to **cease wrathful thoughts** (止息嗔心) and **constantly harbor joy and gladness** (常怀欢喜), **distancing oneself from attachment to self and others** (远离人我), **being benevolent and patient toward all** (慈忍一切), and **remaining serene and tranquil** (恬淡安闲), so that **body and mind may be in harmony** (身心和畅) and **sufferings and diseases do not invade** (病苦不侵).

**The Fourth Precept** is to **cease arrogant thoughts** (止息拓心) and **constantly harbor humility and self-reflection** (常怀退省), **placing others before oneself** (后己先人), **being gentle and refined** (柔软清润), and **speaking skillfully and with ease** (巧说方便), so that **all perceptions and hearings may open one’s wisdom** (一切见闻，悉开智慧).

**The Fifth Precept** is to **cease deluded thoughts** (止息妄心) and **constantly harbor rectitude and stillness** (常怀正静), **contemplating the emptiness of all phenomena** (观想皆空), **remaining pure within and without** (内外清虚), and **aligning with the True Dao** (以合真道), so that **this illusory body may attain liberation** (幻身得度) and **one’s nine ancestral spirits ascend to Heaven** (九祖生天).

The tablet is as follows: Now bestowed upon **the disciple [name] of certain lineage** (某), requesting them to **follow the law faithfully** (如法遵奉). May the **Earthly Officials** (地司) **petition all the Celestial Sovereigns** (保奏诸天) to **record their name in the Ten Directions of the Divine Kings** (十极神王) and the **Four Celestial Officials of the Three Realms** (三界四司), and **announce to the Yin Courts** (告下阴府) that they have **specially transformed their shortened lifespan into extended years** (易短促之年，为延长之算) and **all calamities, diseases, and sufferings are now absolved** (灾苦病患，悉得蠲除). By **steadfastly upholding these precepts** (奉持不退), they shall **gain the protection of the benevolent spirits** (获善神拥护), **abundant blessings and wisdom** (福慧庄严), and **fulfill profound Daoist attainments** (重立玄功), thereby **realizing the Dao of Emptiness** (证虚无道).

Upon receiving this tablet, **let them practice it without slackness** (勿令懈怠). Thus, the tablet is issued.

Year: [blank]
Month: [blank]
Day: [blank]

Given to the **disciple of certain lineage** (某) who has received the precepts.
**Transmitting Master of High Rank** (传度师高功衔):
**The Most Venerable Heavenly Sovereign Who Holds the Fast and Protects the World** (大圣持斋护世天尊),
**The Most Venerable Heavenly Sovereign Who Holds the Precepts and Saves All Beings** (大圣持戒济物天尊).」

**Further Petition to the Daoist Hall for the Eastern Peak’s Record**

**High-Ranked Official’s Name and Status:**
*[Right] Certain [disciple], of the lineage of the Daoist from [Great Ming] country, born in [native place], having entered the Daoist path and completed the rites of sincerity, now stands before the altar to solemnly follow the Daoist rites and perform the *jiao* ceremony. For the disciple *[name]*, I humbly petition before the Celestial Sovereign of the Highest Dao:

*"May the Five Precepts be transmitted to them, that they may wear them with reverence and transform their past deeds into future merit.*

Yet, fearing that this disciple’s *[name]* good deeds are insufficient and their offenses manifold, their karmic ledger is weighed before the Tai Mountain [Eastern Peak] authorities. Should the Netherworld officials indict them, their lifespan may be diminished, and calamities invited. Thus, I submit this petition to the **Heavenly Sovereign of the Eastern Peak, the Imperial Lord of the Celestial Equilibrium and Benevolent Saint**, beseeching Your Sacred Mercy to condescend to their repentance. I pray that You command the Netherworld spirits to **alter their register**, grant them a chance for renewal, extend their years, and remove their afflictions—so that even the most decayed may once more bow to the gift of life.

I dare not presume upon Your Mercy, trembling in awe. This petition is submitted.

*Year [blank] Month [blank] Day [blank]*
*Submitted by [name], holding the rank of High Functionary.*

**Record of the Daoist Hall for Netherworld Re-Registration**
**Ritual Instruments for the *Jiao* Ceremony:**
One jade case for the Eastern Peak’s records, a set of fine ink, brush, and inkstone, all of superior quality.
One hundred sheets of case paper,
Seventy-two divisions of *qian* and *ma* (spirit money) for the Seventy-Two Officials,
Seventy-two brushes,
Seventy-two wooden inkstones,
Seventy-two tally rods, seventy-two inksticks, and seventy-two sheets of case paper.

**Official Record of the Daoist Hall for Re-Registration Before the Seventy-Two Netherworld Judges of the Tai Xuan Capital:**
*"According to their native place and having completed the rites of sincerity, they now stand before the altar for inspection. Their sincerity is evident, and they humbly follow the Daoist rites, seeking protection.*

It is heard that the **Primordial Sovereign’s talismans** contain the saying: *‘There is a way to sever death and gain rebirth.’*
And the **Five Peaks’ Master’s *Longjiao* scripture** states: *‘There is a method to exhaust fate and extend life.’*

Thus, I now invite the lofty immortals to solemnly transmit the **Five Precepts of the Highest Dao** before them, that they may diligently uphold them without slackness, turning back death and prolonging life.

Yet, fearing that the Netherworld officials may still record their offenses and their name remain in the ledger, their guilt unexpiated, and their safety unguaranteed, I now command the preparation of **seventy-two sets of ink, brush, inkstone, tally rods, inksticks, and case paper**, to be offered to the Netherworld authorities. I pray that they **alter the disciple’s *[name]* register**, grant them a new identity, remove their sins from the ledger, absolve their illnesses and misfortunes, and record their merit from upholding the precepts—thus bestowing future blessings upon them.

This record is now issued. Upon receipt, let it be followed without delay.

*Year [blank] Month [blank] Day [blank]*
*Sealed by [name], High Functionary.*

**Judged by the Three Heavenly Exponents of the Orthodox Unity and Auxiliary Mysterious Lord of Tranquil Virtue, Zhang of the Tai Xuan Capital.**
**Proclamation of Yellow Arrow Rites and High-Ranked Ritual Officials**
**Grand Yellow Arrow Fast and Altar Rites**

According to the petitioner, having briefly entered into the intent of the rites and fulfilled the requisite offerings, I now humbly present the Most Venerable and Exalted One’s august and solemn demeanor, which demands the assistance of all officials. Together, we must unite in reverence and harmony to face the Pure Radiance, expound upon the wondrous doctrines, and thus ensure the perfect fulfillment of auspicious rites—fulfilling their due reverence.

The following are the designated roles:

**Ban Shou (班首) Master** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in. The Ban Shou stands above the High Functionary (高功) and must be one of the most virtuous and morally eminent to be selected. If no such person is available, another suitable candidate may be chosen.

**High Functionary (高功) Master** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples, along with their ranks and titles, be filled in. The Six High Functionaries must have received the Great Cavern Arrow (大洞箓) before assuming their roles. If they have not yet received it, then the Lingbao Middle Alliance (灵宝中盟) may also be invoked, for the fasting rites originate from the Lingbao tradition, as established by Master Du of the Celestial Masters.

It is further stated that below the rank of Grand Lecturer (都讲), the title "Master" (法师) is not used, except for the High Functionary alone, who is so called because of the teachings.

**Grand Lecturer (都讲)** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in.

**Supervisor of the Fast (监斋)** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in.

**Attendant of the Scripture (侍经)** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in.

**Attendant of the Incense (侍香)** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in.

**Attendant of the Lamp (侍灯)** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in.

**Keeper of the Gongs and Drums (知磬)** – Request that the names of Daoists from certain prefectures, counties, or temples be filled in.

Additionally, there is the role of **Keeper of the Tablets and Proclamations (知章表)**, for which a young, astute, and melodious individual should be selected. The recitation of Tablets and Proclamations is a critical ritual matter within the fast. If the senior officials are aged, their vision impaired, or their recitation clumsy, errors may arise, leading to irreverence and failing to meet the devout’s intentions.

**Keeper of Offerings (知供养)**, **Bearer of the Hand Censer (执手炉)**, **Directing Official of the Altar (直坛)**, and **Assistant Official of the Altar (佐坛)**—their names shall be provided as needed at the end.

Hereby, I humbly request that each fulfill their duties, uphold the Daoist precepts, and harmonize with the celestial and human realms to attain extraordinary rewards, thus ensuring the perfect completion of the rites without neglect.

*Year [blank] Month [blank] Day [blank]*
*Poster for the Fast and Altar Rites*

**Night Fast Proclamation**

The **Grand Master of Lectures (都讲)** and **Supervisor of the Fast (监斋)**, though not listed by name, shall be included within the scope of the **drum and gong regulations (弹紏之限)**.

**High-Function Master (高功法师)**, surname [blank], seal [blank]
**Chief Disciple (班首法师)**, surname [blank], seal [blank]

**Proclamation for the Night Fast (夜斋榜):**
The Night Fast of *Utilizing Mercy for Salvation (利济)* is established to broadly propagate the Daoist scriptures, rituals, and teachings—all aimed at benefiting the four living beings and the six paths of rebirth. In great fasts of merit, both the living and the departed, all sentient beings, await the blessings of salvation. Thus, the sponsoring masters must cultivate this compassionate intent, universally benefiting the six realms, and not merely adhere to outdated customs by limiting their concern to the *Five Categories of Orphaned Spirits (五姓孤魂)*. This is truly a magnificent and virtuous deed.

Originally, there was no Night Fast Proclamation, but later generations added it—yet their language is often vulgar and lacking in guidance or instruction. Now, we revise and refine it, striving to embody the *Most High’s (太上)* intent of rescue and salvation.

Moreover, in great fasts, the summoning of the *Third Degree (第三度)* spirits is often done hastily—seating them far from the altar, hastily calling them with mere provisions, a brief meal, and then dismissing them with paper offerings. This is far from the intention of allowing them to hear the scriptures and receive the law.

Instead, the departed should be summoned in one night, receive precepts at the altar, and the following night, be provided with *ferry-crossing aid (斛津济)* and further exhorted before being sent off—only then does the grand merit of salvation and deliverance manifest.

For the **Yellow Register Great Fast and Altar (黄箓大斋坛)**, we now establish this proclamation to fulfill the intent of the Most High’s compassionate salvation, extending to all beings in the three realms and the six paths of rebirth, particularly the *Five Categories of Orphaned Spirits* in this realm. We present the *auspicious golden registers and white tablets (吉金箓白简)*, bestow the *Nine True Precepts (九真戒牒)*, and establish the **Most High’s Compassionate Ferry-Crossing Night Fast (太上慈悲津济夜斋)**, thereby expanding the original salvific intent of the altar.

Yet, we now consider that among the spirits recommended—those of the *Heavenly and Human Paths (天人道)*, the *Asura Path (修罗道)*, the *Five-Tone Clans of the Human Path (五音姓人道)*, the *Hellish Officials, Netherworld Clerks, Prison Guards, and Condemned Souls (地狱鬼官、冥吏、狱卒、幽徒)*—there is confusion. Previously, the *Hellish Path (地狱道)* was understood as the realm of suffering spirits, but the *Five-Tone Human Path (五音人道)* also consists of departed souls, risking redundancy. This is because officials and soldiers are included within the *Hellish Path* for the sake of their salvation.

Further, the *Hungry Ghost Path (饿鬼道)* and *Animal Path (旁生道)*—where *animals are born from the side (旁首而生)*, humans from the top (上首而生), and plants from the underside (下首而生), as cited in the *Zhuangzi’s "Master Who Understood the Law" (《庄子·成法师疏注》)*—are deeply mired in the wheel of rebirth, long submerged in the ocean of birth and death. Though their past lives are distant, their karmic distinctions remain. The *Heavenly and Human (天人)* cling to their merits, arrogant in self-pride; the *Asuras (修罗)* are filled with wrath and tyranny, usurping authority; the *Humans (人众)* are misled by wealth, poverty, or fate, failing to cultivate virtue; the *Hellish Officials* are cruel and unmerciful; the *Animals (旁生)* are trapped in other realms, struggling to escape; and the *Hungry Ghosts (饿鬼)*, consumed by insatiable greed, are tormented by flames of hunger.

All are ensnared by their unenlightened nature, causing them to sink into the six paths of suffering. Now, we establish this righteous merit to awaken their inherent nature, urging them to rely on the Dao’s power, sincerely receive the Nine True Precepts, repent their past misdeeds, cultivate pure mindfulness, abandon evil thoughts, and reform their ways—thus attaining awakening within this Dao-field.

Among them, those already liberated should guide the unenlightened, illuminating the path for Heavenly and Human kin, Hellish Officials, and all others, strengthening their virtuous resolve to ascend to higher realms. The *Humans* recognize their inherent goodness, abandoning illusion for truth. Even the *Hungry Ghosts and Animals*, though burdened by deep karmic sins, are granted the opportunity for repentance. All present must heed these teachings, striving to escape the wheel of rebirth and return to the realm of virtue.

Yet, we fear that among them, there may be *rebellious and malevolent spirits (强梁鬼)*, external heretics, or malevolent forces harboring evil intentions, resisting guidance, fostering discord, and terrifying the departed—thus obstructing the righteous rites. Such obstruction must be dispelled through enlightenment.

As before, all are instructed to adhere to these warnings, taking the wheel of birth and death as a mirror to swiftly return to right mindfulness and attain eternal liberation.

Should any *rebellious spirits or malevolent forces (强魂恶爽)* persist in arrogance and defiance, they shall be apprehended by the **Earthly Deities and Local Lords (土地里域主)**, delivered to the **Northern Prison of Tianyi (天乙北狱)**—the bureau overseeing the judgment of ghosts—and punished according to the law, upholding the celestial decrees. All must be aware of this.

*Year [blank] Month [blank] Day [blank]*
*Proclamation for the Night Fast Altar (夜斋坛所)*

**High Master of the Dao** [姓] **seals and transmits the Daoist scriptures and ritual words; the certificate of request reads:**

*"The Daoist disciple, with hands clasped in reverence, submits this oath-word to the Master, pledging with solemn vow to uphold and never betray the sacred trust. When ascending the altar, the Master splits the certificate to transmit the Dao; later generations altered this to four-six rhymed prose, inscribed at the head of the scripture—this was not the original intent of submitting the oath-word. Rather, this word must first be composed before the ritual is performed, then presented to the Master of Transmission.*

*A disciple of the Dao from [native place], born in the year [year], month [month], day [day], now prostrates and submits this word. By fate and karmic ties, I have received the Great Dao. Like a child receiving a talisman, my parents speak for me. If a Daoist priest requests initiation, he shall follow the scriptures previously bestowed upon him, and declare which scripture he now receives—each detail must be clearly stated.*

*With utmost reverence, I present this golden-seal oath-word, humbly offering it to the Master of Transmission. May your compassion, O Master, answer my desperate plea and grant me the honor of receiving these sacred scriptures, that I may wear them as a lifelong treasure.*

*Should I, after receiving them, lightly reveal the profound truths or transmit them to unworthy hands, I shall myself petition the Three Officials for punishment and never dare blame the Dao or the Master.*

*Should I violate this oath-word, I shall be held accountable according to the ritual laws.*

*This is my solemn word.*

*Year [blank] Month [blank] Day [blank]*
*Submitted to the Master of [Scripture] Transmission at [Master’s name]’s door*

**Certificate of Scriptural Transmission**
*Under the reign of [dynasty], in the year of the [zodiac animal], on the [day of the month], [year], [month], [day], the Master of [Scripture], named [name], hereby proclaims to the heavens, earth, watery realms, great mountains and rivers, all responsive numinous spirits, winds, thunder, clouds, and rains—all overseers of this matter—let them bear witness together.*

*Now, a male or female disciple from [state], [county], [village], named [name], born in the year [year], month [month], day [day], devoted to the Dao and joyful in its laws, aspiring to eternal life, now inscribes this oath-word in ink and requests reception of the [Scripture]. I shall follow the ritual faithfully, never daring to disrespect the Master or the Dao, nor betray this oath.*

*Now, I split this certificate into two halves, binding myself before the Three Officials and all saints. If I violate this oath, my spirit shall perish under the Ghost Officials. If I encounter the Three Calamities and Eight Hardships, all tormentors shall assail me. When tested by the Dao, I shall never blame the Way or the Master, but accept my guilt willingly, as decreed by the Most High Laozi.*

*The left half is written in reverse to match the seal. Both halves are five *cun* in length, with the central characters forming the talisman. The right half of the certificate is written on half a sheet of yellow silk, twelve *cun* long, inscribed from both ends, totaling twelve lines. The characters must be written in true red seal script, without cursive strokes or omissions. The talisman fills the center evenly. A golden ring is used, or silver may substitute for silk thread, placed upon the certificate. A seal-engraving tool is used to mark the ring. The Master and disciple now make this covenant, cutting the certificate in two—the Master keeps the left half, the disciple the right, to be kept for life without betrayal.*

**Child’s Protective Talisman**
*The belt is five *zhang* long, dyed in green or purple. Its meaning is that the disciple wears the Master’s teachings as a constant reminder, inscribed upon the sash to ensure it is never forgotten.*

**Proclamation to the Kitchen God and Monastic Officials**
*To the Northern Pole Exorcism Bureau and the Kitchen God of Twenty-Four Spirits:*

*In accordance with ritual intent, I fear that constructing the kitchen altar may involve impure soil or an improper location, or that in daily life, offenses may be committed. Now, through this ritual offering, I also seek atonement. The proclamation is as follows: Please examine my sincere intent and swiftly expel all malevolent *qi* and demonic influences from the dwelling, preventing them from lingering. Drive away all spirits, demons, and malevolent entities, ensuring the residence is pure and serene. Further, I request that each deity take their proper station to protect the inhabitants, warding off fire and theft—both public and private—so that all may dwell in eternal safety. All past offenses shall also be absolved by the righteous law. Upon receiving this proclamation, do not fail to comply.*

*This is the proclamation.*

*Year [blank] Month [blank]*

*Master of the Law* completes the *Dao/Way* Gate’s Canonical Regulations, Volume Ten.
